Archaic period (1500-1000 BC). In addition to the above, the inspection carried out by Seguel (1970) also
recognizes the Quiriquina I and Quiriquina II sites, located around the west coast of the Peninsula of
Talcahuano, corresponding to stratigraphic shells belonging to the Arca period
ico (1500-1000
BC) with lithic artifacts and remains of marine fauna, respectively.
On the other hand, the Concepción 1 discovery was identified by Stehberg (1980) as a cemetery
ceramic with the presence of human burials associated with decorated vessels belonging to the Complex
Cultural El Vergel (1100-1300 AD), as well as the discovery recognized as Río Andalién, characterized
by remains of ceramic vessels and the Chiguayante archaeological site, corresponding to a human burial
with trousseau and offerings (Chizelle et al, 1969), both sites being assigned to said cultural complex.
On the other hand, Seguel (1970) identified the discovery recognized as Quiriquina III, northwest of Quiriquina
I, corresponding to a concentration of ceramic remains, lithic instruments (grinding hands)
corresponding to the Late Pottery Period.
Finally, San Martín (1964) recognizes funereal spaces in the San Pedro de la Paz and Lirquén sites, such as
such as cemeteries, and shell fields with ceramic fragments and/or lithic remains (Lenga and Lirquén), in addition to
conchales without further specifications (Tomé, Centinela and Villa Presidente Ríos), where the majority of
The findings do not present information regarding their chronology, except for Lenga, which corresponds to the Period
Potter, which is added to the Las Chilcas discovery, identified as a ceramic shell (Stehberg, 1980).
In general terms, the archaeological finds reported by said cadastre are concentrated around
to the coast and in association with the courses of the Biobío and Andalién rivers mainly, identifying few
records in the Intermediate Depression for the Biobío region.

3.16.7.5 Results of the Visual Inspection of Archeology
In geomorphological terms, the Area of influence of the Project is located entirely on the flank
western part of the Coastal Mountain Range of the Northwest area of the Biobío Region, which has altitudes not
greater than 300 m.a.s.l. and slopes that fluctuate from low (0-2°) to very steep (over 35°) and
moderately steep (20-30°) (Chapter 3.5. Baseline Geomorphology of the Project).
Various inactive streams are observed in the Project areas, as well as a river course that crosses the
East to West Project (Estero Penco), which gives rise to the growth of dense plant formations in
around its channel. Likewise, the presence of properties with pine forest plantations is observed.
Eucalyptus in much of the Project area, in various stages of growth (from saplings to
mature plantations), associated with which the presence of native forest (maqui, peumo,
Chilean laurel, hualle, boldo, among other species), shrub species and areas with the presence of quila, whose
Coverage varies from open to dense.
In general terms, the presence of forest plantations and the growth of bush vegetation,
trees, quila and/or blackberry associated with them, along with the presence of steep slopes and
Eroded soils resulting from forestry activity constituted access limitations that
strongly conditioned the coverage of archaeological inspection.
Based on a first reconnaissance of the land carried out between August 3 and 4, 2023, as well as
From the analysis of satellite images of the Project area, sectors with
greater and lesser potential for the development of a systematic surface inspection, considering
limitations such as slope and vegetation cover, so inspection activities are
concentrated mainly around the sectors that had a medium to
open and/or sectors with plantations for
recently felled estates, which although not yet cleared
(since they presented remains of felling and clearing of trunks), allowed a systematic tour through
transects. Likewise, sectors with steep slopes (over 25°)6 were discarded from the inspection due to
security reasons, because these slopes, added to the soils eroded by the activity
forestry, with the presence of gullies and risks of landslides, meant a real risk to the
development of the inspection.
To account for the location conditions of non-prospectable sectors (due to slopes
abrupt over 25° and/or with the presence of dense vegetation formations, which constituted
physical barriers insurmountable at the time of the inspection), a total of 172 points of
georeferenced photographic control, the details of which are presented in Annex 3C-48 and Annex 3C-49 of the
6 For the determination of the general slope of the Project area, as well as for the identification and quantification of the
sectors with steep slopes (over 25°, according to the Palma (2018) classification, based on Araya-Vergara and Börgel
(1972), Young (1972) and Ferrando (1993)), a Digital Elevation Model (or DEM) obtained from
from a survey with LIDAR technology carried out by the Project Owner, which presents a spatial resolution of 1
m per pixel. After classifying the DEM raster into slope categories (from none to very steep),
the categories that presented a slope greater than 25°, which were subsequently transformed into polygons for their
mapping and quantification, as presented in the inspection results figures and Appendix 3
of this document.

respectively).

ii. Processing Plant Inspection Results
In the polygon destined for the Commercial Plant, located in the central sector of the Project, the
greater inspection coverage, with 77.33% of its surface (10.13 ha of the total 13.1 ha), without
archaeological finds can be identified, while the non-prospectable sectors correspond to areas
with the presence of Eucalyptus forest plantations with growth of shrub vegetation of
dense coverage inside, as well as areas with remains of
felling of the forest plantation, with presence
accumulation of trunks and branches.
To account for the location conditions of the non-prospectable sectors of this polygon
of the Project, a total of 12 georeferenced photographic control points were recorded, the details of which are
presented in Annex 3C-48 (see Figure 3-31).
Due to the extension and density of the existing forest plantations within this polygon, as well as
as due to the growth of shorter vegetation associated with them, the visual inspection was carried out
from areas cleared of vegetation, corresponding to existing roads, trails,
drilling platforms previously carried out and forestry work areas, corresponding to
steep and stabilized platforms (at least 50 m x 50 m), which allowed evaluating both the
ground surface as exposed stratigraphic profiles (Figure 3-32 to Figure 3-37).
Regarding the evaluation of prospecting factors according to the criteria defined by
Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), visibility in this sector varies from high in clear sectors of
vegetation (roads and forestry work areas) to zero, in sectors with the presence of plantations
forests with growth of dense cover vegetation inside, or in areas with stockpiles
of logging remains, while accessibility is also variable, from high on existing roads
and in work areas, to null in areas with dense vegetation cover and/or with the presence of slopes
steep slope (about 25°).

dense inside.

of the Project, a georeferenced photographic control point was recorded, the details of which are presented in the
Exhibit 3C-48 (Figure 3-38).
Due to the recent felling of the existing forest plantations in this polygon, the inspection
archaeological work concentrated on the sectors cleared of vegetation, which still present, however,
abundant remains of logging (stacked trunks and branches), as well as new shoots of Pine and Eucalyptus and
growth of shrubby vegetation. Likewise, the inspection
n visual was complemented with the tour of
existing roads and forestry work areas, corresponding to steep platforms and
stabilized structures (at least 50 m x 50 m), which allowed evaluating both the surface of the land and
exposed stratigraphic profiles (Figure 3-39 to Figure 3-44).

Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), visibility in this sector varies from high in clear sectors of

of logging remains, while accessibility is also variable, from high on existing roads
and in work areas, to null in areas with dense vegetation cover.

iv. Neptuno disposal zone (ZD) inspection results
In the Neptuno Disposal Zone, located in the Southwest sector of the Project, a low
inspection coverage, with 15.10% of its surface (6.87 ha of the total 45.5 ha), without registering
archaeological finds, while the non-prospectable sectors correspond to areas with
forest plantations and/or wild forest of exotic species (Pine and Acacia), with growth of
bushy or thicket-type vegetation with dense coverage inside. Likewise, areas were observed
recently felled forests, with accumulation of trunks and branches, and sections of ravine with slopes
steep slope (over 25°) associated with forest plantations.
To account for the location conditions of the non-prospectable sectors of this polygon
of the Project, a total of 12 georeferenced photographic control points were recorded, the details of which are
presented in Annex 3C-48 (Figure 3-45).
Due to the extension and density of forest plantations within this polygon, as well as
due to the growth of shorter vegetation associated with them, the visual inspection was carried out
from areas cleared of vegetation, corresponding to existing roads, trails, platforms of
previously carried out drilling and forestry work areas, corresponding to platforms
steep and stabilized (at least 50 m x 50 m), which allowed evaluating both the surface of the
terrain as exposed stratigraphic profiles (Figure 3-46 to Figure 3-51).
Regarding the evaluation of prospecting factors according to the criteria defined by
Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), visibility in this sector varies from high in sectors of
clear of
vegetation (roads and forestry work areas) to zero, in sectors with the presence of plantations
forests with growth of dense cover vegetation inside, or in areas with stockpiles
of logging remains, while accessibility is also variable, from high on existing roads
and in work areas, to null in areas with dense vegetation cover.

that the non-prospectable sectors correspond to areas with the presence of forest plantations of
Eucalyptus or wild forest of exotic species (Eucalyptus and Aromo) with growth of quila and/or
bushy vegetation with dense coverage in its interior, as well as steep slopes (on
25°).

of the Project, a total of 5 georeferenced photographic control points were recorded, the details of which are
presented in Annex 3C-48 (Figure 3-52).

evaluate both the ground surface and exposed stratigraphic profiles (Figure 3-53 to Figure 3-56).

Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), both visibility and accessibility in this sector are practically nil,
achieving access to small portions of the polygon of this work from forest clearings, as well as
from the access road and on the steep platform, which only along its route present a
good visibility and accessibility, observed on both sides of the roads and around the platform
inaccessible areas due to vegetation density (Figure 3-55).

In the Luna Extraction Zone, located at the southeastern end of the Project, a coverage of
inspection of 46.93% (4.13 ha of the total 8.8 ha), without recording archaeological findings, while
that the non-prospectable sectors correspond mainly to areas with the presence of vegetation type
m thicket with dense cover, as well as small patches of Eucalyptus forest plantations with
growth of dense cover vegetation in its interior and areas of steep slopes
(about 25°). It is also observed that the NE limit of this polygon borders the Management Center of
Cemarc waste, which has a slope at the foot of the landfill.
To account for the location conditions of the non-prospectable sectors of this polygon
of the Project, a total of 18 georeferenced photographic control points were recorded, the details of which are
presented in Annex 3C-48 (Figure 3-67).
Due to the dense vegetation cover existing in the area (mainly native type, with
small patches of forest plantations in the Northwest sector of the polygon of this work), the
Visual inspection was carried out from areas cleared of vegetation, corresponding in this case to
access roads to drilling platforms that cross different areas of this polygon, which
They allowed the evaluation of both the ground surface and exposed stratigraphic profiles (Figure 3-68).
Regarding the evaluation of prospecting factors according to the criteria defined by
Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), visibility in this sector varies from high in clear sectors of
vegetation (roads and drilling platforms) to zero, in sectors with the presence of plantations
forests and areas with the presence of dense native vegetation, while accessibility
It is also variable, from high on existing roads and drilling platforms, to zero in areas
with dense vegetation cover and/or with the presence of steep slopes (over 25°) (Figure
3-68 to Figure 3-73).

viii. Road and LTE intervention area inspection results
In the Road Intervention Area (which includes the intervention surfaces associated with roads
projected and to the existing roads with expansion, an inspection coverage of one
65.82% (14.81 ha of the total 22.5 ha11), without recording archaeological finds. The sectors do not
prospects correspond mainly to areas with pine and/or eucalyptus forest plantations with
growth of dense cover vegetation inside, as well as on steep slopes
(over 25°) with the presence of forest plantations (some of them in a mature state, with risk of
falling logs on the accesses due to the slope) and areas with the presence of vegetation of
dense coverage or massive earthworks, close to the Waste Management Center (landfill)
by Cemarc.
Among the existing roads, on the other hand, various typologies are recognized, from narrow roads
enabled exclusively for the transit of light vehicles to wider access roads to the
drilling platforms. Likewise, gravel roads with stabilized material are observed, which connect
the different extraction areas, as well as the main access road from Route 150 towards the Center
of Waste Management (landfill) of Cemarc which, together with a width close to 20 m, presents
paved sections (Figure 3-75 to Figure 3-77).
To account for the location conditions of the non-prospectable sectors of the Area of
Intervention of roads and linear works, a total of 44 photographic control points were recorded
georeferenced, the details of which are presented in Annex 3C-48 (Figure 3-74).
Regarding the evaluation of prospecting factors according to the criteria defined by
Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), visibility in this sector varies from high in clear sectors of
vegetation (existing roads) to zero, in sectors with the presence of forest plantations and areas with
presence of native vegetation with dense cover with projected paths, while accessibility
It is also variable, from high on existing roads, to zero in areas of roads projected with
vegetation with dense cover (forest and/or native) and/or with the presence of steep slopes
(about 25°) (Figure 3-78 to Figure 3-81).

3.16.8 Conclusions
Based on the review of the different documentary sources consulted (registry of archaeological sites
in prioritized MOP basins, specialized magazines, books and congress articles, as well as
environmental evaluation files available in the SEIA, among others), it was determined that no
There are antecedents of archaeological records reported previously within the area of the
Project. The closest archaeological records, previously reported within the framework of the SEIA, are
located at distances of between 191 and 206 m from the Project works, corresponding to the isolated discovery
“El Cabrito 01” - ceramic fragment recorded in the framework of a survey carried out on the occasion of the
“El Cabrito Mining Project”, subsequently entered into evaluation in 2018 under the name
3-103
==================================================================================
PAGE 117
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
“BioLanthanides Project” (which was later withdrawn) and the “Landfill 1” site, reported in the
framework of the EIA of the Project “Operational Continuity Concepción Waste Management Center” (RCA N
202308101534-2023).
In a previous version of the Project layout, it was recorded that the Fill 1 archaeological site was
It was located at a distance of 38m from a planned road. Reason why it was decided
make an intervention request for the execution of boreholes in the area, together with the
subsurface characterization of the PMP-SA-01 site, located inside the Maite Extraction Zone,
works authorized through the ORD. CMN N°1571 of April 3, 2024.
Due to the discovery of an archaeological deposit in the Project area that faced the site
Fill 1, the Owner decided to modify the layout of his works and move the layout 150m to the west.
of the projected road in this area, to reduce possible impacts on the component
archaeological, so the characterization of the site was not continued, since it is no longer part of the
area of influence of the Project (specifically 206m).
Regarding the record “El Cabrito 01”, whose original coordinate would place it 191 m from the closest work
of this Project (North Victoria Extraction Zone), this was not recognized at the time of the
inspection carried out in August 2023. However, as mentioned in the
background, from the review of historical satellite images of the area where said
discovery, it was confirmed that, after its registration in March 2017 (in an area that
presented an adult pine forest plantation), the felling and harvesting of said plantation was carried out,
which most likely meant the removal and/or decontextualization of said isolated finding.
On the other hand, no National Monuments with a declaration were identified within the Project AI.
The closest monument to the Project is located at a distance of 3 km from the works and corresponds to the
Fort La Planchada, Historical Monument located in the commune of Penco.
Regarding the results of the visual archaeological inspection carried out inside the area of the
Project, inspection coverage of 42.40% of the total surface area of the Archeology AI was achieved
(71.73 ha of the total 169.19 ha) through transects separated every 20 m from each other, with percentages of
variable coverage between the different works of the Project, from less than 14% in the Modification of the
Pipeline up to about 77% coverage at the Processing Plant, whose felling and clearing of the
Forest plantation carried out recently allowed a large percentage of co
berture.
In general terms, due to the location of the Project area within the Cordillera de la
Coast of the Biobío Region, the predominance of hills, hills and slopes is observed that
fluctuate from low (0-2°) to very strong (over 35°), with an area of at least 131.29 ha (77.65%
of the total AI) that presents abrupt slopes above 25° (Figure 3-87), which was discarded from the
archaeological inspection for safety reasons, due to the risk of landslide
of soil erosion caused by the existence of forest plantations, as well as by the
difficulties of systematic displacement in these areas.

Cultural Heritage

On the other hand, in addition to the slope, another condition that limited the inspection coverage in the
Project area corresponded to the density of the existing vegetation cover in the work area
projected, which is almost completely parceled out as forest properties with plantations
in different stages of growth currently, from recently felled to adult plantations
ready for harvest. Along with the presence of forest plantations, the presence of dense
plant formations of bush type, scrub and/or quila or blackberry type vegetation that has been
developed both inside the forest properties and around the base of streams, with a
coverage greater than 50%, preventing access and the development of a systematic inspection.
Regarding the evaluation of prospecting factors according to the criteria defined by
Gallardo and Cornejo (1986), the visibility in the Project AI varies from high in clear sectors of
vegetation (roads, drilling platforms and work areas of forest properties) to null, in
sectors with the presence of forest plantations with growth of dense cover vegetation in
its interior, ravine areas with the presence of scrub-type vegetation, wild forest and/or
growth of quila or blackberry-type vegetation, while accessibility is also variable, from
high on existing roads, drilling platforms and forestry work areas, to zero,
in areas with dense vegetation cover and/or with the presence of steep slopes (especially
25°).
Due to the geographical characteristics of the Project Area of Influence and the low accessibility of
certain sections as a result of the slope and the dense vegetation cover, along with the inspection,
made a georeferenced photographic record of control points in all areas that presented
strong access restrictions, preventing a systematic archaeological study through transects.
In order to account for the location conditions of these areas, a total of
172 control points in different non-accessible sections of the Project areas, with coordinates
geographical and panoramic photographs, which were assigned a code (PCA for areal works and PCL for
linear works), as well as a correlative number depending on its location with respect to the works, such as
It is detailed in Appendix 1 of this document. Likewise, Appendix 2 presents
files in Kmz format with details of the control points and photographs of non-prospectable areas
of each work.
Regarding the areas without inspection coverage, those that could not be
inspected only by density of the existing vegetation cover, which adds up to a total of 17.72
ha (10.54% of the total area of the Project), of those areas that have a steep slope
(about 25°), or
well, where the slope and the density of the vegetation cover come together, which add up to 79.46
ha (46.99% of the total surface area of the AI).

Regarding non-prospectable areas that showed low accessibility and visibility due to the presence
of forest plantations, wild forest and/or areas with scrub or shrub-type vegetation (18,31
ha, as detailed in Table 3-9 and in Annex 3C-48 of this document – as “Area without
inspection coverage due to dense vegetation"), it is proposed to carry out a microrouting through
equidistant transects separated every 10 m from each other, once the favorable RCA of the Project has been obtained and
after cleaning the land and clearing the vegetation. Said visual inspection must be
carried out by an archaeologist or graduate in Archeology and implemented after
the logging, removal and cleaning activities of vegetation in each area of the Project and prior to any
type of escarpment, excavation or deposit of materials on the surface due to the Project works.
Regarding surfaces that present access limitations due to both dense vegetation and
steep slope (79.89 ha), it is proposed to carry out Permanent Archaeological Monitoring of the
vegetation clearing activities, because the slope and soil erosion resulting from the
forestry activity does not allow a systematic route, even once the surface vegetation has been cleared.
From these activities, it must be sent to the Superintendence of the Environment (SMA) and the CMN.
a new visual inspection report of the areas pending due to dense vegetation, with a minimum of 2
months in advance of the start of works in those sectors, having to wait for the approval of the CMN
to begin the Project works in the areas pending inspection.
From the inspection carried out, only one archaeological site was recognized, called PMP-SA-
01, corresponding to a concentration of ceramic fragments from smoothed surfaces (interior and
exterior) of 146 m2, of possible historical temporality of indigenous tradition (judging by the presence of
fragments of smoothed surfaces, without lathe marks and with the use of antiplastics of the aggregate type
fine granulometry, although clearly visible), located inside the Maite ZE, in the area of a road
existing.
Depending on the characteristics and location of the archaeological records – both previous and current
inspection – regarding the Project works, as well as from the results of the characterization
subsurface through drilling wells from the PMP-SA-01 site and the Project area that faced the
Fill 1 site (as authorized in ORD. CMN 1571-2024 and whose results are presented in the
Annex 3C-52 of this EIA), the following measures are proposed (Table 3-10):
- Regarding the isolated discovery “El Cabrito 01”, because it is located more than 190 m from the work
closest and because it was not identified during the inspection, it is not considered necessary to
carrying out new measures, because no nearby records were identified in said area.

Project area and the low visibility and general accessibility, the implementation of a

The monitoring must be carried out by an archaeologist(s) and/or a graduate(s) in archaeology,

any type of surface removal and/or excavation. Along with this, talks should be held

at the end of the month, which will include the following information:
a) Description of the activities on all excavation fronts for the month, with date.
b) Description of matrix and materiality found (with depth) in each excavation work.
c) Monthly work plan of the construction company where the days are specified in the work book
monitored by the archaeologist and the work fronts monitored in said period.
d) Plans and photos (high resolution) of the different excavation fronts and their different
e) stages of progress.
f) Contents of the induction talks held and the consistency of attendees with the
g) signature of each worker.
h) If archaeological remains are evident, incorporate:
a. Archaeological record sheet with panoramic and specific photographs of the findings
(in high resolution).
b. Detailed description of the state of conservation and if there was any impact due to the works of the
project.
c. Protection and/or conservation measures implemented.
d. Proof of notification of the discovery to the National Monuments Council, in accordance with
what is established in art. 26 of Law 17,288 on National Monuments.
i) Monitor the state of conservation of the prevention measures to be implemented
if applicable (fencing, signage, etc.).
j) The final monitoring report must account for the activities carried out, and if they have been
detected archaeological sites, include the corresponding rescue information. In these cases
A bibliographic review of the area will be included, the analysis (by type of materiality) and the
conservation of all archaeological materials
ics that are the reason for this activity.

Ultimately, the archaeological intervention permit must be requested, according to Article 7 of the
Excavation Regulations, established in Law 17,288 of National Monuments.

indicated at the time of delivering the final monitoring report, for which, a

3.17 Cultural Heritage (Paleontology)
3.17.1 Introduction
This report presents the baseline study of paleontology in the area of influence of the
Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Earth Concentrate
Raras (hereinafter, the Project), located approximately 15 km northeast of the city of Concepción
and 1 km southeast of the city of Penco (measured from the closest part of the Project), in order to
establish the presence of fossiliferous elements in the geological units associated with the area and estimate the
impact that the Project could imply on them. This report documents the realization of said
study, whose complementary work in the field was carried out between June 10 and 12, 2019.
This section provides the characterization of the paleontology component of the area of influence.
of the Project, in accordance with the provisions of article 18 literal e.5) of the SEIA Regulations, D.S.
N°40/2012, modified through D.S N° 30/2023, both from the Ministry of the Environment, as
established in Law No. 19,300 on General Environmental Bases, Law No. 17,288 of
National Monuments (modified in Law No. 21,215), also following what is indicated by the Guide to
Paleontological Reports (2016) of the National Monuments Council.
3.17.2 Objectives
3.17.2.1 General Objective
Carry out the characterization or baseline study that allows establishing the paleontological potential
of the lithological units of the Project's area of influence.
3.17.2.2 Specific Objectives
• Carry out a visual inspection on the ground, which allows determining the geological units
present records
n fossil elements.
• Evaluate the possible impact of fossil remains on the surface and in the excavation area or
projected earth movements.
• Prepare a paleontological report for the entire area of influence of the Project following
strictly the guidelines indicated in the “Guide to Paleontological Reports” of the Council of
Natural Monuments (CMN, 2017).

3.17.3 Area of influence
For the baseline of the paleontological heritage component, the area of influence underlies only
in the Project intervention areas: extraction zones (ZE), deposit zone (ZD),
vegetable collection (ZAV), processing plant area, stockpile, existing roads to improve and roads
projected, covering a total area of 169.19 hectares. (Figure-3-88).
In accordance with the provisions of Title I, article 2, referred to the definitions of the System Regulations
of Environmental Impact Assessment (D.S. 40/12), in letter a) the area of Influence is defined as: “a) The area
or geographical space, whose attributes, natural or sociocultural elements must be considered with
the purpose of defining whether the project or activity generates or presents any of the effects, characteristics or
circumstances of article 11 of the Law, or to justify the non-existence of said effects,
characteristics or circumstances.” It is for this reason that the area of influence (AI) considered in the
This characterization of Cultural Heritage includes the effective surfaces of the works, which are
detailed in Table 3-11 and Figure-3-88.

3.17.4 Methodology
The methodology applied in this work considered the indications contained in the “Guide to Reports
Paleontological” of the National Monuments Council, published in 2017. The sources of
Information can be classified into three groups, described in the points below:
3.17.4.1 Bibliographic Information
A review and analysis of the technical-scientific literature available for the area of influence was carried out.
located in the Cosmito sector, 15 km north of Concepción, Biobío Region. Within said
literature includes undergraduate thesis work in geology on the area of potential intervention
(Inostroza, 2018), technical-geological literature delivered by the Project owner (Marquardt and Belmar,
2017) and the Concepción-Chillán Sheet on a scale of 1:250,000 prepared by SERNAGEOMIN (Gajardo, 1981).
3.17.4.2 Field inspection and Project information
Based on the information
information available about the Project (geological drilling, projected
Project earthworks and geological profiles), a field campaign was carried out from 10
until June 12, 2019. To access and travel through the area of influence of the Project, a
4 X 4 traction vehicle. The field inspection was developed giving emphasis to sectors where
contemplates the development of earth moving or excavation activities.
In this way, the inspected area covered 3,088 km2, within which 48 points of inspection were established.
paleontological inspection (Figure-3-89). For the entire area of influence, and beyond its limits,
Road cuts, exposed slopes of natural water drops, surrounding areas, and edge were reviewed.
coastal, in order to characterize the distribution of stratigraphic units on the surface and subsoil.
Specific inspection points were photographed and referenced, based on their
geological and paleontological representativeness (Table 3-12). The search routes (path traveled to
the search for fossils) were drawn in situ considering the characteristics of the terrain, maximizing
obtaining paleontological information. During the development of the inspection, no
paleontological excavations nor was any type of fossil material extracted from the ground.

With the information obtained from the bibliographic review and field inspection, we seek to establish the
paleontological potential in accordance with the guidelines of the “Paleontological Report Guide”
prepared by CMN, 2017, which establishes the following:
• Sterile (low to no paleontological potential): Units that correspond to intrusive bodies and
high temperature and high energy volcanic products, except certain types of ignimbrites. In case
of having a sedimentary unit without bibliographical history of the presence of fossils and that in
terrain has been found to have no fossils or sedimentological characteristics conducive to
have them (e.g. highly energetic debris flow of large blocks), may be included in this
category.
• Susceptible (low to medium paleontological potential): Sedimentary and volcano-
sedimentary with facies, with the possibility of containing fossils,
even though they lack
bibliographic paleontological background. From the sedimentological point of view, it is
facies that, due to the sedimentary environment they represent, could house remains
paleontological. Also included in this category are geological units that have been
3-121

PAGE 135
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
mapped with a scale of little detail and does not allow us to locate where the
susceptible and/or fossiliferous levels.
• Fossiliferous (medium to high paleontological potential): These are sedimentary units and
volcano-sedimentary, in which their fossiliferous content has previously been reported, both
in the literature (scientific articles and summaries, SEIA, etc.), such as during visual inspection in
ground.
3.17.5 Results
3.17.5.1 Paleontological Assessments within the SEIA Framework
A total of 103 project files submitted for environmental evaluation were reviewed (approved, in
qualification, rejected or not admitted for processing) located up to 20 km away from the area of the
Project, among which are port, road, real estate, mining development and
of waste management, among others (Table 3-13), of which 94 do not present baselines of the
component under analysis.
Of the 9 projects that presented information surveys of the paleontological component 6,
reported positive results in terms of the recording of findings, due to the location of these
on sedimentary lithological unit, on or near the coastline.

3.17.5.2
Geological Context
The Project area is located 15 km east of the city of Concepción and 3km east of the city of Penco.
The inspected area has an area of 3,088 km2 and is located on a rock complex
metamorphic and igneous rocks of the Paleozoic era. Figure-3-90 shows a geological map underlying
that of the Project area.
3-136
==================================================================================
PAGE 150
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Figure-3-90: Geological map of the area of influence. The inspection points and route are contrasted
Source: District Geology Project
3-137
==================================================================================
PAGE 151
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
i. Metamorphic Unit (Devonian-Early Triassic Age)
It extends approximately between 34° and 47° south latitude along the Coastal Mountain Range. Said
component has been divided into two series according to its lithological, structural and
degree of metamorphism (Aguirre et al., 1972). Eastern Series and Western Series; both constitute the
called Paired Metamorphic Belt (González-Bonorino and Aguirre, 1970; Aguirre and others, 1972; Hervé,
1977; Hervé, 1988), defined by Miyashiro (1961). The “Oriental Series” is composed of a sequence
of metapelites and metapsamites, which have been interpreted as turbiditic sediments deposited in
a deep marine forearc environment (Cartes, 2004), between the Devonian and early Carboniferous,
in a context of passive margin (Hervé, 1988) (Figure-3-90).
The “Western Series”, not outcropping in the area, is composed mainly of quartz schists,
feldspar (nodular albite schists), micaschists, metachert, greenschists (metabasites) and
some serpentinitic bodies. These rocks are metamorphosed to greenschist facies and,
In some sectors, transitions to blueschist facies are observed, produced by basal accretion
initial (Vásquez, 2001), which is evidenced by the presence of glaucophane throughout the series (Aguirre &
others, 1972).
Between the city of Concepción and the Nahuelbuta Mountain Range, Vásquez (2001) determined a degree of
Barrovian type metamorphism of medium to intermediate P/T, to which a metamorphism is superimposed
Buchan type of low pressure and high temperature, associated with the intrusion of coastal batholith of the
Late Paleozoic (Hervé, 1977; Vásquez, 2001; Cartes, 2004). This last thermal event generated a
mineral zonation parallel to the batholith that goes from biotite zone, andalusite zone, to
sillimanite closest to this igneous body. According to dating carried out in the Lirquén area
by Lucassen & others (2004) in which they corroborate the thermal effects of the intrusion of the batholith in the
Eastern Series, ages of 298±8 Ma are calculated (Inostroza, 2018).
ii. Intrusive Unit (Upper Carboniferous-Upper Triassic age)
The intrusive rocks in this area are represented by the Coastal Batholith of South Central Chile, the
which extends from Valparaíso to the Lanalhue Fault zone (37°- 38° South Lat.) in a strip with
NNE-SSW orientation (Hervé & others, 1987). These rocks have been assigned to the Carboniferous period.
Permian (Hervé & others, 1987), however, intrusives from the Upper Triassic also crop out in the zone.
(Hervé, 1988) and the Jurassic (Gajardo, 1981).
The South Central Coastal Batholith is mainly composed of granodiorites and tonalites of
hornblende and biotite (Parada, 1990; Creixel, 2001), with sectors of quartz diorites and granites. This
intrusive body is zoned laterally, in it, granodiorites and tonalites form the
centrally and towards the edges, more differentiated rocks develop (Creixel, 2001; Inostroza, 2018). Creixel
(2001), proposes subdividing the Coastal Batholith into 3 subunits; Tonalites of Santa Juana, the Granitoids
3-138
==================================================================================
PAGE 152
================
==================================================================

Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
of Nahuelbuta and Granitoids of Concepción. This last batholith is located in the urban area of the city
of Concepción, composed mainly of biotite monzogranites, biotite tonalites, and
muscovite, outcropping in the northern sector of Concepción, it is also possible to find hypabyssal rocks
of tonalitic composition (Inostroza, 2018) (Figure-3-90).
To the east of the city of Penco, the Penco Plutonic Complex is present, informally defined by the
Geology team of the Aclara Project. This complex is mainly made up of phaneritic rocks.
medium to coarse grained equigranular. The units of this sector are made up of rocks of composition
garnet granites, diorites and quartz diorites (Figure-3-90). Minor bodies instruct the Unit
Penco, dikes with preferential NW orientations of dioritic composition, are widely distributed in the
north of Penco, between Rafael and Menque (see Biolantanidos, 2018). Alternatively, an intrusive drive,
Biotite Granite is recognized in this area. This unit is made up mainly of rocks
medium to coarse grained equigranular phaneritic, locally porphyritic, Composed of tonalites,
granodiorites and granites; all with abundant biotite. To a lesser extent, bodies of
pegmatites in Poñen and quartz diorite in Punta Culín (310 Ma.; Deckhart, 2014). The minor intrusions
of this unit include granitic dikes (see Biolantanidos, 2018).
iii. Sedimentary Rocks
These lithological units are mentioned in this report in order to provide a geological context.
regional. However, they are not part of and/or do not emerge in sectors close to the area of influence of the
project, therefore, there is no impact on the fossil units.
Quiriquina Formation: Defined by Biro & others (1982) and described as a siliciclastic sequence
deposited in a marine environment in the Upper Cretaceous. Its type locality was established in Bahía Las
Tablas, on Quiriquina Island, and its paratype locality in Caleta Cocholgüe. The lithology of this formation,
described in its type locality, consists of a basal conglomerate, yellow sandstones, coquina levels and
sandstone area with calcareous concretions (Salazar, 2004). The maximum recognized power is in the
outcrops from its type locality, in Bahía las Tablas, with a thickness of 65 m (Salazar, 2004). The age of
This formation was determined based on its fossiliferous content. Biró (1982) assigns it to the Campanian-
Maastrichtian and Stinnesbeck (1986) propose Maastrichtian age; Finally Salazar (2004) restricts it
to the Upper Maastrichtian.
These rocks are arranged in unconformity on the metamorphic rocks of the Eastern Series and the
Granitoids of Concepción and underlies concordant to the Curanilahue Formation and in paraconformity to
the Quaternary deposits (Salazar, 2004). For his part, Galli (1967) expresses an agreement between the
Cretaceous rocks and the Tertiary layers assigned to the Cosmito Formation.
Curanilahue Formation: The Curanilahue Formation consists of a continental sedimentary sequence,
Consisting mainly of sandstones, partly conglomeratic and claystones associated with mantles
3-139
==================================================================================
PAGE 153
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
carboniferous, with marine intercalations, corresponding to fossiliferous green sandstones (Pineda, 1983).
The estimated power of this formation is 500 m (Muñoz-Cristi, 1968).
Curanilahue Formation was initially described by Muñoz-Cristi (1946) calling it “Floor
Curalinahue”, and categorized into four horizons: Pilpilco, Lota and Colico. Later, Muñoz-Cristi
(1948), formalizes this unit calling it, Curanilahue Formation.
In 1968, Muñoz Cristi differentiated purely continental rocks from those of marine origin, this is how
also, definitively upgrades the former Pilpilco Member to the Pilpilco Formation and divides its
once to Curanilahue Formation, in three members: Member Lota, Member
ro Intercalation and Member Colic
(Inostroza 2018). Based on the fossiliferous content of gastropods and bivalves present in the Member
Intercalation (marine) (although not reported in Cosmito), Muñoz Cristi (1956), assigns Formation
Curanilahue to the Lower Eocene.
The Curanilahue Formation is correlated with the Cosmito Formation defined by Galli (1967) due to
its lithological similarities (García, 1968) and with the Cerro Alto Formation defined by Frutos (1982) on the Island
Quiriquina. Curanilahue Formation overlies concordantly on the Pilpilco and Quiriquina formations, and
in unconformity (currently unconformity) on the metamorphic basement (Pineda, 1983; Inostroza
2018).
The Curanilahue Formation is arranged in a strip parallel to the west of the Quiriquina Formation and the
Metamorphic Basement (Figure 7.1), in Arauco Bay, Carampangue River, Trongol River, Antíguala
(Tavera, 1942; Muñoz-Cristi, 1946 and 1968; García, 1968; Blanco & others, 1974 in Pineda, 1983). The
Lota and Colico members are wedged towards the West and the Intercalation Member becomes more important
in that direction (Pineda, 1983).
Around the study area, Curanilahue Formation (Old Cosmito Formation) (Inostroza 2018) is
extends to the North of the Biobío River, in a NE-SW direction, from Lirquén (Puerto Lirquén, Sector
Tierras Coloradas and Sector Cosmito) to Laguna Redonda (García, 2004). In addition to emerging in the form
discontinuous in the Lo Pequén Sector, in some island hills of Concepción, in Talcahuano and along
the coastal area in Dichato, Coliumo, Punta Montecristo, Cocholgüe, Caleta Matanza, Punta de Parra,
Penco and Lirquén (Intercalation Member) (Inostroza 2018). In Concepción it is observed in Cerro Amarillo,
in the Bellavista sector, at the Cosmito station and in Cantera Parque del memoria. In Talcahuano it is presented
at CAP Stadium, Cerro David Fuentes, El Bosque sector, Morro de Talcahuano. They are also identified
important outcrops on the road that connects Concepción, Penco and Lirquén, and on the Itata Route
(Inostroza 2018).
In some sectors it is possible to identify that the Curanilahue Formation lies in nonconformity to the
Metamorphic Basement (at the exit of the Itata Route) and in other sectors, the Curanilahue Formation
3-140
==================================================================================

==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
(originally Cosmito Formation) is found unconformably under the Andalién Formation (Cantera Parque
del memoria) or in contact with unconsolidated deposits (Galli, 1967, Inostroza 2018).
The three members that make up the Curanilahue Formation are described below, based on the
classification proposed by (Inostroza 2018):
Colico Member: it crops out in the Penco-Lirquén Bypass, this Member of continental origin, made up of
conglomerates at the base, followed by fine and coarse sandstones, shales and clays with lagoonal character in
which are interspersed by 5 coal seams. Towards the roof it is composed of fine-grained sandstones
thick. Its thickness varies from 90 to 130 m. Like the Lota Member, it wedges westward in
together with the coal seams. The environment is interpreted as fluvial with lagoon episodes
(Pineda, 1983, Inostroza 2018).
Galli (1967), on the other hand, defines the Cosmito Formation (Curanilahue Formation according to Inostroza 2018),
which is made up of shale, conglomerate sandstone and coal, where the shale and sandstone
predominate and in most of the outcrops they are very altered with a yellowish color
characteristic reddish. The shale is partly carbonaceous, fissile and is associated with coal seams of the type
lignite (Galli, 1967). This sequence reaches a maximum power of 130 m (Galli, 1967, Inostroza, 2018).
Its outcrops are diverse; in the Las Pataguas sector, Penco Bypass, in the O'Higgins Underpass of the
Penco-Lirquén Bypass, Itata Route entrance, Lafquén Pass, Cerro Amarillo of the Hualpén commune,
Cosmito Station, Bellavista sector, Cerro Amarillo de Concepción, among others (see Inostroza 2018).
Cosmito Formation: Defined by Galli (1967) at the Cosmito Railway Station, located 5 km to the North
of Concepción. Its lithology is made up of shale, sandstone
s conglomerates and coal, where the shale
and sandstone predominate and in most of the outcrops they are very altered with a
characteristic reddish yellowish color. The shale is partly carbonaceous, fissile and is associated with mantles of
lignite type coal (Galli, 1967). The lithological correlation made with the Curanilahue Formation
defined in Arauco allows us to date this formation to the Eocene (Galli, 1967). Its best outcrops are
They are located in Villa Cocholgüe, entrance to Cocholgüe, Punta Montecristo, Miramar, Cosmito and in Penco
(Interport Highway). The Cosmito Formation is arranged concordantly on the Quiriquina Formation
and underlies the Andalién Formation or Quaternary deposits in angular unconformity (Galli, 1967). The
maximum power is 130 m and the environment corresponds to lagoon, coastal deposits associated with
swamps and coastal dunes, formed in a low energy environment (Galli, 1967; Pineda, 1983; Inostroza,
2018).
In the Penco-Lirquén bypass, the Colico Member emerges, this member of continental origin, which
It consists of conglomerates at the base, followed by fine and coarse sandstones, shales and clays with
lagoon character in which 5 coal seams are interspersed. Towards the roof it is composed of sandstone
from fine to coarse grain. Inostroza (2008), establishes that the Cosmito and Curanilahue Formation could be
considered the same unit given their lithological characteristics.

Andalién Formation: Defined by Galli (1967), made up of a set of sandstones and conglomerates.
polymictic in the type area located in the low mountain ranges distributed between Cerro Verde, located to the west
of Concepción and the city of Penco. These rocks were described as sediment deposits of type
torrential in a continental foothills environment. The calculated thickness is approximately 30 m
(Galli, 1967). It overlies in angular discordance on Paleogene rocks and underlies in the same way
the sediments of the Huachipato Formation (García, 2004). For this formation, a Pliocene age is estimated.
to Pleistocene, given the comparison with rock formations in Arauco, which cover a terrace, between 50
and 100 m higher than the adjacent Pliocene plateau (Brüggen, 1950 in Galli, 1967).
iv. Analysis and Geological Context of the Project Influence Area
The Project is developed on residual soils generated from intrusive igneous rocks and
metamorphic. These rocks underwent intense physical and chemical weathering processes, generating a
weathered level called “saprolite”, which is characterized by the loss of cohesion between its
minerals and an increase in clay content in alterable minerals. This weathered profile reaches
a thickness between 40 and 60 meters. According to Reading (1999), the special characteristics of these soils are
a response from the combination of environments related to climate, rainfall, humidity regimes
temperature, the lithology of the parent rock material, water movement, drainage conditions,
the relief, the vegetation, the age of the weathering levels, among other factors. A profile of
Development of this type of saprolites is schematically summarized below in Figure-3-91.
Figure-3-91: Stratigraphic Column prepared in the field (Section ZE Victoria)
Source: Aclara
The saprolite is mainly composed of a combination of kaolin-type clays, quartz, granites and
micas; giving the profile a characteristic reddish yellowish color, due to the minerals with Fe.

Rare Earth Concentrate
Due to their residual origin from intrusive and to a lesser extent metamorphic rocks, these soils do not
present favorable conditions for fossilization. In this sense, the probability of registering
fossiliferous elements in the area of influence
nce of the Clay Extraction Mining Development Project
for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate, is low and/or nil.
3.17.5.3 Paleontological background
Regarding the paleontological background within the geological area where the Project is inserted, it is
incorporated antecedents at a regional level corresponding to the fossil content of the Formation
Curanilahue, Quiriquina Formation and some descriptions of finds for the Metamorphic Unit-Series
Eastern.
General paleontological background obtained from bibliography is indicated below:
Metamorphic Unit-Oriental Series: Regarding the Oriental Series of this unit, according to Bandel and
Quinzio-Sinn (1999), the presence of trace fossils in laminated slate from the Eastern Series has been described.
of the Metamorphic Basement. This discovery was made north of the town of Lirquén.
They were probably the product of crustacean activity (isopods, ostracods and chelicerates).
merostomates) from lacustrine environments.
Quiriquina Formation: For the Quiriquina Formation, from the Upper Cretaceous, around
150 fossil species corresponding to fish, reptiles, birds, cephalopods, gastropods, scaphopods,
bivalves, crustaceans, bryozoans, annelids, hexacoralids, foraminifera and plants. They have also been
At least 23 ichnotaxa corresponding to 18 ichngenera have been identified (Escobar et al., 1977).
Curanilahue Formation: According to the antecedents consulted (Ferraris, 1981; Muñoz, 1968) in this
formation, from the lower Eocene, an abundant flora has been described in the Lota and Colico members.
The presence of marine fauna has also been documented in the Intercalación member. Some of the
Foraminiferal species present in the Intercalation member correspond to the Melania species
araucana, Frondicularia capitana, Nodosaria affinis.

3.17.5.5 Paleontological Potential of the Project influence area
Based on the information contained in the Geological Chart (Gajardo, 1981), the district geology and
inspection carried out on the ground, it is then possible to indicate the lithological units in the vicinity and
in the area of influence of the Project, regarding its potential and in turn paleontological category (Table
3-14).

PRP: Previous paleontological records; AAP: Crops in the Project area
Source: Aclara
According to the above, of the six lithological units present in the Penco area, only one of them outcrops
in the area of influence of the Project, which corresponds to the intrusive rocks that make up the Complex
Plutonic Penco. Due to its intrusive nature, this lithological unit would exhibit a potential
paleontological Null to Low. Consequently, this unit is paleontologically categorized as
Sterile. Finally, it is emphasized that the project will be located in areas only with the presence of

saprolitic soil, resulting from the physical and chemical weathering that occurred in said igneous basement, which
makes the occurrence of fossil material unlikely.
3.17.6 Conclusions
According to the lithological characteristics and origin of the geological components existing in the area of
influence for the Paleontology component, of the works of the Mining Development Project of
Extraction of Clays for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate, it is concluded that the potential
paleontological area is sterile (Low to Null), in accordance with the criteria established by the Council
of National Monuments (CMN). This conclusion is weighed under the following arguments:
• The lithology present in the area where the Project will be developed is formed by weathering
chemistry and physics due to seasonal weather conditions. The resulting residual minerals
of weathering are: clays (mainly kaolinite), quartz, garnet and micas (biotite). The rock
met
eorized is known by the name “Saprolite”, which is distributed as a semi-mantle
horizontal than in the Project area which has a vertical thickness of 40 to 60 m. About the Saprolite
organic soils are developed.
• The Project is located on heavily weathered intrusive and metamorphic rocks. The
plutonic basement is made up of Diorite, Garnet Granite and Biotite Granite, while
that the metamorphic unit is represented by metapelite-type rocks. The surface levels of
These rocks undergo the weathering process, generating an altered level or saprolite.
• The area in which the Project will be located is already an area subject to high levels of disturbance,
such as excavations and earth movement due to the high industrial activity resulting from the transfer
of garbage to the nearby landfill, and by the forestry activity present in the area.
• No fossiliferous material was observed in the lithological units that underlie the area of influence of the
Project. Other nearby sedimentary units (>4 km) crop out outside the area of influence, such as:
Curanilahue, Cosmito, Andalien Formation and/or Quiriquina Formation, if they record fossiliferous material,
However, no contact is recognized between the sedimentary units and the unit
plutonic/metamorphic in the area in which the project is located. Alternatively, neither
evidence transport of material from the sedimentary units.
Consequently, it is determined that the characteristics of the intrusive-metamorphic units of the area of
influence in which the Project will take place do not record fossil specimens, so its impact does not
It is significant. The Project area would be made up of components resulting from weathering
physics and chemistry occurred to the basal and igneous metamorphic basement (saprolite), which makes it unlikely
the occurrence of fossil material. In this sense, it is classified as Sterile (null paleontological potential at
Low) to the entire area of influence for this component.

3.18 Landscape
3.18.1 Introduction
In accordance with the provisions of Law No. 19,300 on General Bases of the Environment and
Regulation of the Environmental Assessment System (D.S. N°40/2012, modified by D.S. N° 30/2023,
both of the MMA), Paragraph 2° Article 18 literal e.6, this report provides the characterization
of the landscape component for the area of influence of the Mineral Extraction Development Project
Clays for Rare Earth Concentrate Production”, through the description of type variables or
character13, visibility14 and quality15 of the landscape.
Article 9 of the aforementioned Regulation defines that “an area has landscape value when, being perceptible
Visually, it has natural attributes that give it a quality that makes it unique and representative.”
In accordance with the above, this Baseline has been prepared considering the indicated contents
by the Environmental Assessment Service in the “Guide for the environmental impact assessment of the value
landscape in the SEIA” (SEA, 2019), which includes, within its methodology, the characterization of the landscape
through the recognition of its character and the description of its basic components
cos. Subsequently,
The visual quality of the landscape is evaluated, taking into account the biophysical, aesthetic and structural attributes
of the units that make it up.
3.18.2 Objectives
3.18.2.1 General Objective
Determine the landscape value of the Area of Influence of the Mining Development Project for the Extraction of
Clays for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate (hereinafter “the Project”), in accordance with the
established in the Guide for the Environmental Impact Assessment of Landscape Value in the SEIA (SEA 2019),
through the fulfillment of the specific objectives, indicated below.
3.18.2.2 Specific Objectives
• Characterize the landscape of the Project Area of Influence
• Define the visibility of the works and parts of the Project
13 Character of the landscape: it is defined as that recognizable identity in a certain landscape, which arises from the perception of
a pattern associated with the combination of its biophysical, aesthetic and structural attributes, which make it unique and differentiate it
of other landscapes.
14 The visibility of a landscape depends fundamentally on its topographic and atmospheric conditions and the distance
with respect to the observation point.
15 Within the framework of the SEIA, visual quality is defined as the degree of excellence or merit that a certain landscape presents, the
which is determined based on the analysis and assessment of its attributes that make it unique and representative.
3-161
==================================================================================
PAGE 175
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
• Rate the visual quality of the Landscape
3.18.3 Methodology
The methodology for evaluating landscape value and visual quality is based on the “Guide for the
Environmental Impact Assessment of Landscape Value in the SEIA” of the year 2019 (hereinafter “Guide to
Landscape”), whose methodological steps are described below.
3.18.3.1 Preliminary analysis
In this stage, a bibliographic review is carried out on landscape aspects of the Project area,
including the hierarchy of the landscape and the analysis of assumptions that allowed the macrozones to be defined16
and landscape subzones17 to identify, in a preliminary and general way, the character of the landscape.
Furthermore, on a cartographic model and with the help of Google Earth Pro® software, the
possible observation points and viewsheds present in the Project location area,
depending on its layout, access roads and the geomorphology of the area. Observation points (PO)
They should be located in the sectors with the greatest access for any observer. Due to the above, the
Selection of the OPs considers the following criteria defined in the SEA landscape guide:
• Views from the main road axes, taking into account the average daily intensity of the flow of
transport as an indicator of the frequency of observers.
• Views from panoramic viewpoints located on roads and trails.
• In urban areas, views where there is a high potential of observers. Within the framework of the
present Baseline, this criterion extends to rural areas, considering the presence of
localities, homes and agro-industrial facilities dispersed in the territory where it is located
the Project.
3.18.3.2 Terrain campaign
A field campaign was carried out between December 5 and 6, 2022, in which the area was toured
where the Project is located, particularly through 150, 152 and Route O-390.
During the tour of the area, the visual attributes of the landscape were identified, for which they were used and rectified.
the observation points previously defined in the cabinet stage, depending on the characteristics
of the landscape and location of the parts of the Project.
16 Landscape macrozones are large extensions delimited by geographical elements, coinciding with the regions
bioclimatic characteristics of the country and have a visual character determined by the dominance of some of its biophysical attributes.
17 Landscape subzones are the second hierarchical level of landscape and coincide with the main geoforms of the territory.

3.18.3.3 Application of the Landscape Guide
After the field campaign, the reconstruction of the territory was carried out through the organization of the
photographic record and the coordinates of the observation points (PO) erected in the area of the
Project. The characterization and evaluation of the landscape was carried out based on the methodology established in the
“Guide for the Environmental Impact Assessment of Landscape Value in the SEIA” (SEA, 2019), namely:
i. Determination of the landscape value of the area where the Project is located
It was carried out through the characterization of the landscape, based on the recognition of its character, which is
function of the macrozone and subzone of landscape where the parts and works of the Project are located, and the
dominance of some visual biophysical attributes. The elements are understood as biophysical attributes.
relief, soil, water, vegetation, fauna and snow that, according to their individual variables and their assessment,
characterize the Landscape.

a) Determination of observation points
For the selection of potential observation points, the following criteria are considered, according to the
“Guide for the Environmental Impact Assessment of Landscape Value in the SEIA (SEA 2019)”:
• The main routes and roads that allow physical and visual access to the Project area.
• Populated locations or concentrations of observers.
• Points that, due to their panoramic and visibility characteristics, are constituted as
current and potential viewpoints.
During the field work, a tour and on-site validation of the main routes and roads was carried out.
with visual access in the direction of the Project, the previously determined observation points were confirmed
to the terrain, and new observation points were identified and georeferenced, based on what was seen
on the ground once inserted in the area of influence.
b) Delimitation of viewsheds and intervisibility analysis
The landscape analysis is based on the visibility condition of a given area (in this case the area
of the Project), the viewshed being understood as the portion of land visible from a certain
observation point.
The viewsheds are defined based on the visibility or visual range that is available from the points of
observation identified in office activities and during the field campaign, due to their

panoramic, accessibility and visibility characteristics in the direction of the parts and works of the Project,
as if they were habitually visited by a common observer.
The viewsheds were generated by using ArcGIS 10® Software, in the Viewshed module,
which automatically delivers the viewshed from a point or route, depending on the
topographic characteristics obtained through a Digital Terrain Model or DEM. Taking into account
Taking into account what is stated in the Landscape Guide, it is considered the maximum or critical distance of visual range.
3,500 m, since from that distance the observer stops perceiving an object clearly
determined.
Subsequently, the viewsheds were characterized based on their shape, size, view types and
compactness (or number of unseen areas).
Meanwhile, intervisibility is understood as the degree of reciprocal visibility between a series of points.
of observation and contemplates the calculation of the total of the visible areas from each observation point. “The
Overlaying the viewshed maps of all observation points results in
the map of the area of influence” (SEA, 2019:44).

a) Identification of landscape units
The first step to determine visual quality is to identify the landscape units (PU) included.
in the AI. Landscape units are spatial divisions, and their identification and delimitation refers to the
recognition of portions of the territory that have a homogeneous appearance, which is a result of
the combination of its biophysical, aesthetic and structural visual attributes. Homogeneity can
be sought in the repetition of forms or in the combination of some similar features, but not
necessarily identical (SEA,2019).

3.18.4 Area of Influence
In accordance with the methodology established in the Guide for the Environmental Impact Assessment of the Value
Landscape in the SEIA (2019), the polygon of the Area of Influence of the Landscape component is the result of
the superposition of the maps of the viewsheds of the evaluated observation points.
Based on the above, the landscape influence area corresponds to the area from where the different
parts and facilities of the Project could be visually perceptible, or where the visual quality
could be affected by its parts, works and/or activities.
This area is defined from the visual access resulting from each viewshed, which represents by
On the one hand, those elements of the relief, constructions or various obstacles that affect the areas
visible from each observation point, and on the other hand have been established from a visual distance
of 3,500 m, corresponding to the maximum limit at which an observer stops clearly perceiving a
given object. The resulting area is shown below in Figure 3-110.
The surface of the Area of Influence was defined from the intervisibility analysis resulting from the
combination of each viewshed, where a maximum visual distance of 3,500 m was determined for each
observation point, giving rise to visible areas according to relief, height and environmental conditions
(tree curtains and vegetation mainly). As mentioned in the previous point, the extension
The Area of Influence refers to the visible areas that are configured from each Point of Influence.

3.18.5 Results
3.18.5.1 Determination of the landscape value of the area where the
Project
i. Identification of the macrozone and subzone of the landscape where the
Project
The project is located in the communes of Penco and Concepción, Province of Concepción, Biobío Region,
Specifically, it is located in the Coihueco Farm sector, located on part of the Cordillera de la Sierra.
Coast. Its main access is via Route 150, in front of the town of La Greda. Depending on your location, the
Project is located in the Central Macrozone and in the Coastal Edge Subzone as can be seen in the Figure
3-111.
Figure 3-111. Location of the Project within the Central Macrozone and Coastal Edge Subzone.
Source: GAC
The Central Macrozone extends from the Aconcagua River to the Biobío River, covering the regions of
Valparaíso (south), Metropolitan of Santiago, Del Libertador General Bernardo O'Higgins, Maule, Ñuble and
3-175
==================================================================================
PAGE 189
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Biobío (north). The character of the landscape is determined by the dominance of urban areas, the
which are located mainly in valley bottoms and slopes with moderate slopes constitute
homogeneous areas totally occupied by urban, agricultural or forest lands. Naturalness is seen
progressively restricted to the areas of the La Costa and Los Andes mountain ranges, where
They find diverse and valuable ecosystems (SEA, 2019).
Visibility and intervisibility conditions generally determine a lower degree of exposure of the
territory, which is reduced by the morphology of the territory itself, by the presence of vegetation of
medium and large magnitude and by occasional episodes of fog and cloudiness. The visual basins
They acquire a compact shape, with limited depth of field as a result of variations in the
relief and vegetation (SEA, 2019). Climatic conditions show landscapes that change texture
and colors according to the moderate seasonality that characterizes the central area.
Regarding the Subzone, geomorphologically speaking, the project area is located in an area of
transition between the Coastal Mountain Range and the Coastal Edge, in a sector described by Börgel (1983) as
the Central Region of the Basins and the Fluvio-Glacio-Volcanic Plain, where the coastline is generally
mixed, presenting extensive beaches of sandy accumulation combined with sections of cliffs.
On the other hand, the features of the Coastal Mountain Range, in the lower reaches of the Itata River, the mountain range
is diluted in complex reliefs, of low height, signifying a topography transformed into hills that
They advance both towards the coast and towards the interior of the territory.
The commune of Penco presents transitional climatic characteristics between the Mediterranean climate and the
humid temperate climate that predominates towards the south, is influenced by the effects of the mountain range of
the coast, where it acts as a climate screen in relation to how the temperature and the
precipitation (Municipality of Penco, 2019e); These conditions occur in the coastal strip and in
the high sectors and western slopes of the Coastal Mountain Range, with constant humidity (INERCO,
2018). Precipitation is concentrated preferably in winter, increasing from north to south, and from
west to east, product of the presence of frontal systems (Errázuriz, 1998).
The hydrographic system of the Commune is made up of the Penco and Lirquén Wetlands, and part of the River
Andalién, which in turn is the southern limit of the Commune. In
Regarding the Estero Penco, it should be noted that
This is located in the Central Urban Zone and has an approximate length of 6 km. It is born in the Zones
Altas de Penco and receives the main contribution from natural rainwater springs. His influence and
use in agricultural activities is minimal since it registers its greatest flow in the urban area,
area in which it is channeled (Municipality of Penco, 2019e).
In the domain of temperate climates, of the Mediterranean type, there is the biogeographic unit “Zona
subhumid with a predominance of mesophytic, shrubby and arboreal vegetation”, which develops between the
regions of Valparaíso and Concepción (Errázuriz, 1998) and has a transition zone from the area
Mediterranean to temperate from the Maule River (MNHN, 2015). In this area there are forests

Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of

typical of the Mediterranean area such as the sclerophyllous forest and also others of the hygrophilous region, such as the
oak.
According to the vegetation classification of Gajardo (1994), the Project location area is
located in the Deciduous Forest Region, specifically in the Deciduous Forest Sub-Region
of the Llano, in the Formation of the Deciduous Forests of Concepción, which represents the forests of
deciduous leaves, occupying the central depression and the low-altitude mountainous reliefs, until reaching the
coast in some sectors (INERCO, 2018).
According to the vegetation floors of Luebert & Pliscoff (2006), in the communal area 2
floors, one of the Coastal Temperate Mediterranean Deciduous Forest of Oak and Sclerophyllous Forest
Mediterranean Coastal Litre and Azara integrifolia. It is worth mentioning that the original flora has gone
changing as a result of forest productive development, currently being the dominant formation,
surpassing the native forest and arborescent scrub and being replaced by species of pine and
eucalyptus.
ii. Demarcation of the Project site
As mentioned previously, the Project is located in the communes of Penco and Concepción,
province of Concepción, Biobío Region, specifically located in the Fundo Coihueco sector, the
which is located on a low mountain range that is part of the Coastal Mountain Range.
Its main access is via Route 150, in front of the town of La Greda.
As for the main geomorphological units that the communal territory presents, there is the cord
western part of the Cordillera de La Costa, where eroded reliefs such as mountain ranges stand out,
accumulation reliefs, such as valleys, local terraces and hydromorphic plains. The topography of the commune
It is rugged, alternating ranges of hills and ravines. In turn, the slopes are presented on
25% and the elevations, with respect to mean sea level, fluctuate between 30 and 200 meters (GORE Biobío,
2014a).
Biogeographically, the landscape is diverse and three general ecosystems are observed: the mountain range, the
wetlands, and the coastal ecosystem, which includes beaches and estuary. Particularly, the project is located in
the coastal mountain range ecosystem, which has a large extension in the territory of Penco, which
It is characterized by being mainly occupied by forest plantations, among which,
You can also find some small areas of native forest, which houses various
species of flora and fauna. Regarding the small relicts of native forest, there is the forest of
Queule, which will not be intervened by the Project, and which is associated upstream of the estuary
Penco and a second formation located between Penco and Tomé, which concentrates endemic trees in
danger of extinction that were believed to be lost in the Region (Municipality of Penco, 2019e).

The area
The location of the Project is located on the peaks of the western flank of the Cordillera
from the Coast, at an average altitude of 220 meters above sea level. Currently, a large part of the areas where
Project facilities are planned, they are covered with forest plantations, existing
For this reason, a large number of access roads throughout the sector. Part of the access road from

homes in a large part of the metropolitan area, however, being private it does not imply the income of

plant, clay processing plant, the stockpile for the temporary collection of material prior to

In general, the relief of this area is characterized by presenting biophysical, aesthetic and
structures typical of the coastal landscape of the central-southern zone of the country, where the successive alternation of
mountain ranges, beaches and abrupt coastal cuts, are combined with ocher tones to
highlight the gentle hills in contrast with the rocky outcrops and the development of important
vegetation and forest plantations present in the area. The views are usually clear, where the
panoramic view of the landscape is imposed almost without natural visual barriers, however, there are various
anthropic visual barriers in the area, which generate visual obstructions to specific points.

iii. Identification and description of biophysical attributes
To define the landscape characteristics of the environment surrounding the project, one can speak of a
rural cultural landscape (Muñoz Pedreros, 2013) characterized by presenting profound changes in the matrix
original naturalness, being replaced by productive activities, which in the case of the Cordillera
of the Coast in the central and southern area of the country, corresponds mainly to forest plantations.
Below are described these attributes that characterize the territories where the Project is located:
• Relief: it is constituted as a structuring element, where in the eyes of a common observer, the
Views are made, in general, from sectors of lower altitude (urban area, main routes), where
There are terraces and plains that prominently observe the visible face of the coastal mountain range,
which does not exceed 200 meters above sea level. The slopes are greater than 15% and in some cases exceed the
30%.
• Soil: is marked by the respective uses of the territory, dominated by pine plantations
and eucalyptus, in some cases growing and in other cases already harvested. In these last cases,
The soil adopts a coarse grain resulting from the residue of clear felling. However, regarding the area
observed from public routes, in general the plantations are located behind strips of
diverse tree and shrub vegetation, a situation that prevents direct access to bare soil, which
which translates into a medium roughness.
• Vegetation: There is a high vegetation cover, with a dominance of forestry monoculture and
small patches of native, tree and shrub vegetation that precede the plantations of
pines and eucalyptus. Its foliage is permanent.
• Water: this is not directly observed, although the closest water course corresponds to the
Penco estuary, which in PO3 is located approximately
80 m in a northerly direction. By having a
coastal edge location, visual access to the sea is possible only through the highest levels of
the city.
• Fauna: this attribute is relevant, to the extent that only birds and domestic animals are observed,
but in low abundance and diversity.
• Snow: this attribute is not common for the coastal area and was not observed during the field visit.

to ground.
