iii. Intervisibility Analysis
As defined in the methodology, intervisibility is understood as the degree of reciprocal visibility
between a series of observation points and contemplates the calculation of the total of the visible areas from each
PO. It is obtained from the sum of the visible areas of the viewsheds, showing the areas visually
most exposed areas of a territory, which results in the map of the Project Area of Influence.
In Figure-3-115 you can see the intervisibility modeling obtained from the combination of the
viewsheds for each observation point.

3.18.5.3 Determination of the visual quality of the landscape in the area of influence
i. Identification of landscape units
As mentioned above, the UP are portions of the territory that have a
homogeneous, which is the result of the combination of its visual attributes. Inside the surface
identified as the Area of influence of the Project, two landscape units (UP) were established, whose
The main differences correspond to the characteristics of their biophysical attributes derived from the soil and
the vegetal cover.
The determination of the Landscape Units responded to the recognition of portions of the territory that
They have a homogeneous appearance, resulting from the combination of their biophysical visual attributes,
aesthetic and structural. The above is supported by the selection of representative photographs that
are shown in Table-3-19.
Regarding the procedure, landscape units are established on the basis of visual aspects or
that give character to the factors considered as defining or main of the landscape, which refers us to
to the results of point 3.18.5.1, where it was determined that the attributes that give value to the landscape
correspond to the relief and vegetation, having as an additional element the views towards the coast with
access to the sea.
In this way the homogeneous units were determined from the primary component of each
unit, corresponding to the most representative and the secondary one, the one that underlies the main attribute, and
Homogeneous areas were subsequently mapped based on the primary element. The
homogeneity of each one is evident from the repetition of forms or the combination of features
similar, but not necessarily identical (Guide for the Environmental Impact Assessment of the Value
Landscape in the SEIA, SEA 2019).
Next, the landscape units are identified according to the most representative attributes of
each homogeneous area:
▪ UP1 Coastal mountain range with monoculture plantation and other plant formations.
▪ UP2 Urbanized areas on coastal terraces.

3.18.6 Conclusions
The Mining Development Project of Clay Extraction for the Production of Earth Concentrate
Rare, it is located in the communes of Penco and Concepción, province of Concepción, Biobío Region,
specifically located in the sector of the Coihueco Fund, which is located on a ridge
low mountain range that is part of the Coastal Mountain Range. Its main access is through
Route 150, in front of the town of La Greda, and, additionally, access through
Route 152.
According to the landscape assumptions described for the national territory, its location corresponds to
the Central Macrozone and the Coastal Edge Subzone.
The character of the landscape and its value are determined by attributes of abiotic origin (relief and
soil) and vegetation, with no relevant findings identified in water (at least in the environment close to the
Project) or fauna, corresponding mainly to a rural cultural landscape, whose original matrix of
naturalness has been replaced by forestry activities.
The development of the viewsheds was carried out on the basis of 10 Observation Points distributed
on the main access roads that surround the project: Routes 150, 152 and O-390, where
3-199
==================================================================================
PAGE 213
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
urban sectors such as Cosmito, La Greda and the main entrance to the Estero Penco Trail, access
private. Given the morphology of the sector, the presence of forest plantations is important, the watersheds
visuals turned out to be irregular and elongated in shape, medium and large in size, with low and medium
compactness and largely focused views. From the resulting area of influence, 2 units were distinguished
landscape: UP1 Coastal mountain range with monoculture plantation and other plant formations, and UP2
Urbanized areas on coastal terraces.
The analysis of visual quality applied to each landscape unit resulted in the area of
influence has a Medium visual quality, where UP1 obtained a Medium rating and UP2 a
low rating. According to the aesthetic and structural biophysical attributes, they present a low
uniqueness and diversity of elements, where their visual quality is common in accordance with the
landscape assumptions defined for the Central Macrozone and Coastal Edge Subzone.
The landscape and tourism components may be affected by future changes in patterns of
precipitation and temperature. Review changes in precipitation and temperature patterns described
for flora and vegetation components, wildlife and the hydrology, hydrogeology and
water quality.
Regarding the climate risks potentially applicable to the landscape and tourism components, it is worth noting
the increase in the risk of fires and the increase in the risk of loss of greenery in native forests,
as indicated in Table 3-25 and Table 3-26. These risks can potentially alter the quality
visual of the landscape and the tourist value of the territory.

3.19 Protected Areas and Priority Sites
3.19.1 Introduction
Below is the report that includes the results referring to the Protected Areas, Areas
Placed Under Official Protection (ACBPO) and Priority Sites, applicable to the Mining Development Project
of Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate, based on the provisions of the
current regulations, specifically in the Regulation of the Environmental Impact Assessment System
(RSEIA), D.S. No. 40/2012 modified through D.S. No. 30/2023, both of the MMA, and as established in
Law No. 19,300 on General Environmental Bases.
Based on the above, it is important to specify that the Protected Areas are defined by the Article
8° of the RSEIA, as “any portions of territory, geographically delimited and established
through an administrative act of a competent authority, placed under protection
official tion with the
purpose of ensuring biological diversity, protecting the preservation of nature or conserving the
environmental heritage." To understand the relationship between the parts, works and activities of the Project with
said portions of the territory and their relevance within the SEIA, is that the provisions were considered
present in article 3 of the RSEIA and articles 10 and 11 of Law No. 19,300. The above is detailed in
continued:
• Article 3 - RSEIA and Article 10 - Law No. 19,300: Which determines those “projects or activities
likely to cause environmental impact, in any of their phases, which must be subject to the
environmental impact evaluation system.” In relation to protected areas and areas
placed under official protection, the relevant provisions are contained in literal p),
which specifies the “execution of works, programs or activities in areas that are part of the
National System of Protected Areas, urban wetlands and in other areas placed under
official protection, in cases where the respective legislation allows it.”
• Article 11 - Law No. 19,300: Which determines “the projects or activities listed in the article
precedent will require the preparation of an Environmental Impact Study, if they generate or present
at least one of the following effects, characteristics or circumstances”, being relevant to
of this component, literal d), which specifies that for the preparation of a Study
of Environmental Impact, the “location in or close to towns, resources and areas” will be relevant.
protected areas, priority sites for conservation, protected wetlands, glaciers and areas with
value for astronomical observation for scientific research purposes, likely to be
affected, as well as the environmental value of the territory22 in which it is intended to be located.”
22 According to the RSEIA article 8, territorial Environmental Value is understood as: “the Territory with no or low anthropic intervention
and provides local ecosystem services relevant to the population, or whose ecosystems or natural formations present
characteristics of uniqueness, scarcity or representativeness.”

influence of the component and its surroundings.
• Describe the protected areas and priority sites that are in or close to the area of protection.
influence of the component and its surroundings.
3.19.3 Area of influence
For the delimitation of the area of influence, the provisions of Article 8 of the RSEIA have been considered.
where it is established that, to present an Imp Study
Environmental Act, the project must comply with
the following requirements; namely:
- If the Project or activity is located in populations, resources, protected areas, priority sites
for conservation, protected wetlands and glaciers, which are susceptible to being affected,
as well as the environmental value of the territory in which it is intended to be located;
- If the project is located close to populations, resources, protected areas, priority sites for
conservation, protected wetlands and glaciers, susceptible to being affected, as well as the value
environment of the territory in which it is intended to be located.

Additionally, in order to evaluate whether the Project or activity affects protected areas, areas placed under

that “the extension, magnitude or duration of the intervention of its parts, works or actions will be considered,
as well as the impacts generated by the Project or activity, taking into special consideration the
protection objects that are intended to be protected.” Depending on what is stipulated in the article,
establish the following definitions in order to identify possible effects:
• Next: “It will be understood that the Project or activity is located in or close to a town,
protected resources and areas, priority sites for conservation, protected wetlands,
glaciers or a territory with environmental value, when these are in the area of
influence of the Project or activity.”
• Protected areas: as “any portion of territory, geographically delimited and
established by administrative act of a competent authority, placed under
official protection with the purpose of ensuring biological diversity, protecting the preservation
of nature or conserve environmental heritage.”

main justification the following provision expressed in the cited article of the RSEIA:
• Affectation of the environmental value due to the impacts generated by the parts, works and/or
Project actions.

of the parts, works and actions. Associated with:
• The location of the parts, works and actions of the Project within a protected area,
area placed under official protection or a priority site for conservation.

In accordance with the provisions of article 8 of the RSEIA, “Protected Areas” are defined as
“any portions of territory, geographically delimited and established by an act
administrative authority of competent authority, placed under official protection in order to ensure
biological diversity, protect the preservation of nature or conserve environmental heritage.”

techniques on areas placed under official protection and protected areas for the purposes of the Protection System.
Environmental Impact Assessment” (hereinafter, Instruction No. 130844), identifies the categories of
“protected areas” referred to in literal d) of article 11 of Law No. 19,300.

ii. Areas Placed Under Official Protection
In accordance with what is indicated in instructions No. 130844, Law No. 19,300, the RSEIA defines what must be
be understood as “areas placed under official protection”, however, the same concept allows
identify the elements that define it. For this reason, it can be noted that said area corresponds
to a delimited geographical space, which has an official declaration and that said declaration
responds, directly or indirectly, to an object of environmental protection.
In this regard, the aforementioned instructions identify the categories of “areas placed under official protection”
to which literal p) of article 10 of Law No. 19,300 refers, incorporating through the instructions
OF. ORD. N°202099102647/2020 and N°161081/2016, of the SEA, the categories “Wetlands declared
priority sites for the conservation of biodiversity”, “Historical conservation properties”,
“Conservation Zones” and “Areas for the protection of resources of natural value, dictated subject to
the General Urban Planning and Construction Ordinance -OGUC-”.

iii. Priority Sites for Biodiversity Conservation
Priority sites for biodiversity conservation are another name for natural areas.
with environmental value considered in article 11 letter d of Law 19,300 on General Environmental Bases
Environment.
The office Ord. No. 103008/10 of the National Commission of the Environment (CONAMA) indicates that these
“constitute terrestrial, marine or coastal-marine areas of high value for conservation and use
sustainable biodiversity, identified by its contribution to ecosystem representativeness, by its
ecological singularity or for constituting a habitat for threatened species, among other aspects, for their
conservation, protection and/or restoration management. Such sites may, to the extent possible,
to become protected areas.” In turn, this instruction officializes a list of priority sites
defined within the framework of the National Biodiversity Strategy by CONAMA, which have not yet been
placed under official protection and that must be considered within the framework of the SEIA. Said list of 64
sites nationwide was updated by the Of. Ord. OF. N°100143/10 of the SEA.

published by the Area of Natural Resources and Biodiversity, SEREMI of the Environment Region of the
Biobío Planning and Development Division of the Regional Government of Biobío.

and/or link with the delimited AI. The statement is broken down below:
• Protected Areas: based on the territorial analysis carried out, it is possible to point out that, within the Area
of Influence, no protected areas are identified, the closest area is located 8 kilometers away, the
which corresponds to the “Nonguén National Park”, followed by the Nature Sanctuary
Biobío River Mouth” 10 kilometers away and “Hualpén Peninsula Nature Sanctuary”
11 kilometers away.
• Areas placed under official protection: based on the territorial analysis carried out, it is possible to indicate
that, within the area of influence of the Project, ACBPOs are not identified, considering the
presence of Historical Conservation Properties, Historical Monuments, followed by Zones of
Historic Conservation and Wetlands, which are concentrated in the urban areas of the region,
not presenting interaction with the parts and works of the Project, being at a distance
more than a kilometer of these.
• Priority Sites: based on the territorial analysis carried out, it is possible to point out that the Area of
Influence of the Project does not intersect with the priority sites, the closest is 4.2
kilometers “Rocuant Andalién Wetland”, incorporated in OF.ORD N°18.0369 of 26
January 2018. On the other hand, according to the priority sites without effects of the SEIA, no
within the proposed AI, the closest to it being the National Priority Site
corresponding to the Regional Biodiversity Strategy of the Biobío region: “Wetlands System
Concepción Intercomunal Lake” located 10.4 kilometers away.

3.20 Natural or cultural attractions and their interrelationships (Tourism)
3.20.1 Introduction
This report will allow us to know the current state of the natural or cultural attractions and their
interrelationships that attract flows of visitors or tourists to the area of influence of the “Project of
Mining Development of Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate” (hereinafter
“the Project”), which will be located in the commune of Penco and Concepción, in the province of Concepción,
Biobío region, and its relationship with the planned activities and works.
In this way, the characterization of the component will be carried out based on the requirements of the
Environmental Impact Assessment System, within the framework of what is established by Law No. 19,300 on Bases
General Environmental Regulations and their subsequent modifications, and specifically, letter e.8) of the
Article 18 of the D.S. N°40 of 2012 of the Ministry of the Environment, which modified the Regulation of the
Environmental Impact Assessment System (RSEIA).
Article 9 of the same Regulation defines that “an area has tourist value when, having value
landscape, cultural and/or heritage, attracts flows of visitors or tourists to it.” In accordance with the
above, this Baseline has been prepared considering the contents requested by the Service
of Environmental Assessment in the Environmental Impact Assessment Guide, Tourist Value in the SEIA (2017),
which includes within the methodology the survey of natural or cultural attractions, the
tourist heritage and the attraction of visitors or tourists.
3.20.2 Objectives
3.20.2.1 General Objective
Identify and describe the Tourist Value of the project's area of influence through characterization
of the cultural, landscape and heritage value, and the existence of flows of visitors or tourists in the sector,
in accordance with the provisions of the “Guide for Environmental Impact Assessment Tourist Value” in the SEIA
(2017), through the fulfillment of the specific objectives indicated below:
3.20.2.2 Specific objectives
• Characterize the landscape24, cultural and heritage value in the tourist dynamics of the communes
involved in the Project.
24 Uses the results of the Landscape Baseline as input data, according to the method established in the Evaluation Guide
of Environmental Impact Landscape Value in the SEIA (SEA, 2019), in addition to the natural attractions present in the
territory.
3-225
==================================================================================
PAGE 239
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
• Identify the existence of a flow of visitors or tourists in the communal tourism dynamics and in the
area of influence.
• Determine the Tourist Value of the Influence Area.
3.20.3 Methodology
This Baseline was developed systematically considering the scope indicated in the
Tourist Value Environmental Impact Assessment Guide in the SEIA (2017). For the above, it was used
secondary information and a collection of information in the field, which made it possible to complement the
information obtained from the background check.
The methodology of this report is addressed at the following levels of analysis:
• Project Area: Corresponds to the parts, works and actions of the Project.
• Study Area: In the case of this document, it will be understood as those communes in which
The parts, works and actions of the Project are established, or those that are relevant from
include in tourist terms.
• Area of Influence: Territory where the impacts of the
project, in relation to the Tourism component.
The methodological steps carried out for the execution of this present are described below.
document.
3.20.3.1 First stage of cabinet
It corresponds to a preliminary bibliographic search of different sources of tourist information
available regarding tourist attractions, tourist offer, tourist circuits, SIMBIO, ZOIT and other areas
protection, terrestrial connectivity and infrastructure and support equipment for tourism activity.
The objective of this stage is mainly to identify potential tourist places and activities.
close to the study area in order to visit them during the field campaign.
3.20.3.2 Terrain campaign
The work during the field campaign mainly includes two tasks, photographic recording and
location (with GPS) of attractions, tourist services, infrastructure and tourist support equipment.
On the other hand, the tourism and territorial planning offices will be visited, in order to compile
official information about the tourist dynamics of the territory and its main attractions.
The field campaign was carried out on Monday, December 12 and Tuesday, December 13, 2022.

3.20.3.3 Second cabinet stage
In this stage, the information collected is analyzed and complemented with data and information from
specific character that allow us to demonstrate that a specific area has scenic, cultural or
patrimonial, and what is the degree of that value (high, medium or low). The indications are considered for this
of the “Environmental Impact Assessment Guide: Tourist Value in the SEIA” of the SEA (2017).
3.20.3.4 Definition of Tourist Value
In order to determine the Tourist Value of an area, this can be done based on an equation that
combines the attributes of Landscape Value, Cultural Value and Heritage Value, which can be found
singularly or in combination. Additionally, one, two or three of the attributes must be presented next to the factor
“attracts flows of visitors or tourists”, this point being an essential condition regarding the
determination of the Tourist Value, since the attraction of visitors is in turn inherent to the activity
tourist. It should be noted that this attribute must be considered under its current scenario and not before one
potential or future (Figure 3-125):
Figure 3-125. Definition Tourist Value
Source: SEA (2017).
Below are the parameters that allow establishing each attribute that defines the Value
Tourist:
i. Landscape Value
The identification of the landscape value of an area is determined by considering the results obtained
obtained in the Landscape Value report, in accordance with the methodology established in the “Guide to
Environmental Impact Assessment: Landscape Value in the SEIA” (SEA 2019), whose application allows
establish whether an area has landscape value in consideration of the biophysical attributes presented by the
studied territory.
Of
In a complementary way, the attractions of the natural sites category, defined
as “places in the area in question considered due to their interest as landscape, excluding
any other criteria, such as equipment or recreational activities” according to OAS-CICATUR25. These
25 Organization of American States – Inter-American Tourism Training Center.

Attractions include mountains (hills, volcanoes, ravines, glaciers, etc.), plains (plains,
deserts, dunes, salt flats, etc.), coasts (beaches, cliffs, gulfs, islands, fjords, etc.), bodies of water
(lakes, rivers), protected areas and places to observe flora and fauna, hot springs, places of interest
geological and paleontological, grottos or caverns and hunting and fishing places.
For this, the presence of attractions categorized as “natural sites” of the Cadastre of
SERNATUR Tourist Attractions, or any other natural attraction that supports activities
tourist due to the value of its landscape.
ii. Cultural Value
It is understood that an area has Cultural Value when there are material elements (furniture
or real estate) or intangible assets that are of special interest from a historical point of view,
archaeological, traditional, spiritual, artistic, aesthetic, social, technical and/or scientific. Operationally,
It is determined that an area has cultural value when it has tourist attractions of a cultural nature.
To obtain this information you can use the Cadastre of Tourist Attractions prepared by the
SERNATUR (2019), where all categories except for “Natural Sites” are considered
cultural tourist attractions. You can also use the records held by municipalities or other
entities in the study area, or collect information in situ from a field campaign.
Taking as reference the SERNATUR Registry of Tourist Attractions, the cultural character is
understood as all those expressions such as:
• Museums, cultural events and places of historical or cultural interest
• Folklore
• Recreation center or place
• Contemporary technical, scientific or artistic realization and historical cultural
• Scheduled events
• Tourist routes and circuits
iii. Asset Value
Within the framework of the SEA tourism guide, an area has heritage value when it
They develop tourist services or activities that meet two fundamental requirements:
• That the service or activity is consistent with the concepts of value and heritage. It must be
understand “value” as that which has a “degree of usefulness or aptitude to satisfy

“a set of assets belonging to a natural or legal person or assigned to a purpose,
susceptible to economic estimation”27. The above is understood in the fact that both the
Services such as tourist activities constitute value and are heritage of an area, linked to
the attraction of flow of visitors or tourists.

iv. Attraction of flow of visitors or tourists
The attribute that attracts flow corresponds to a characteristic composed of two elements: the action of
attract and flow, so it is interpreted that the condition attracts flows of visitors or tourists to the
area of interest, be it a current attribute and not a potential or future one. On the other hand, the concept of visitor
refers to a person who travels to a main destination other than their usual environment, for example
a duration of less than one year, for any main purpose (leisure, business or other personal reason)
that is not employed by an entity resident in the country or location visited. A visitor is classified as
tourist (or overnight visitor) if your trip includes an overnight stay.
This attribute is determined based on information from primary or secondary sources, where the
magnitude of the flow is estimated through the review of available statistics on overnight stays in
tourist accommodation establishments, or through interviews with authorities, representatives
or inhabitants of the studied area, who can account for the presence or flow of visitors or tourists,
independent of its magnitude. The reviewed background must allow us to analyze and evaluate that

3.20.4 Area of Influence
The tourist value is an attribute that receives possible impacts or activities that take place in the area.
territory, for which it is necessary to define what the scope of the Project will be in tourist terms
considering its parts, works and actions. In order to establish which portions of the territory associated with the
Project, will be recognized as an area of influence, the units that
present tourist value (Cultural Value and/or Heritage Value and/or Landscape Value + Attraction and flow of
visitors or tourists).
As mentioned above, the communal context where the tourism dynamics is analyzed, in this
case corresponds to the commune of Penco and Concepción, which provides the bases for later
determine an area of influence in terms of tourist value, where the Project could effectively
manifest impacts in relation to the Tourism component. In this way, the analysis will be generally
to the particular, and the tourist assessment will be carried out on the final area of influence.
To determine the area of influence, and in the context of the “Tourist Value Guide in the SEIA 2017”, it must be
specify a surface in spatial terms, clearly and accurately indicating its limits. Likewise
Likewise, information must be provided that explains and substantiates its determination. Of
According to the above, to delimit the AI, the existence of the following elements must be known in
the characterization area:
i. Landscape Value
This is determined through the preparation of the Landscape Study, according to the “Landscape Value Guide in
the SEIA 2019”. This is a document prior to this report and its results are used as input.
In addition, the attractive “natural sites” of the SERNATUR Tourist Attractions Registry will be considered.
ii. Tourist attractions and activities present in the study area
For this purpose, the SERNATUR Cadastre of Tourist Attractions of a cultural type will be used, information
tourism of the Municipalities, providers of tourist services, among others, in order to represent the
cultural and heritage value of the area of influence.
iii. Access routes
The public access road network is incorporated, since they will be the connecting routes for tourists and
visitors.

3.20.5 Results
3.20.5.1 Project Location
The sector
where the Project is located corresponds to the commune of Penco and Concepción, Region of the
Biobío, specifically located in the Coihueco Fund sector, located on part of the Cordillera
coastal. Its main access is via Route 150, in front of the town of La Greda.
In accordance with the regional tourism dynamics, part of the communal territory of Penco is located within
of the Tourist Destination (SERNATUR, 2018) “Concepción and surroundings”, a delimitation that also includes
part of the project works, as seen in Figure 3-129.
Figure 3-129. Project location area
Source: GAC
3.20.5.2 Landscape Value
According to the landscape assumptions described for the national territory (SEA, 2019), the location
of the project corresponds to the Central Macrozone and the Coastal Edge Subzone.
3-236
==================================================================================
PAGE 250
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
The character of the landscape of the Central Macrozone is determined by the dominance of areas
urban, which are located mainly in valley bottoms and slopes with moderate slopes
which constitute homogeneous areas totally occupied by urban, agricultural or forest lands. The
naturalness is progressively restricted towards the areas of the La Costa and Los Andes mountain ranges,
where diverse and valuable ecosystems are found (SEA, 2019).
On the other hand, visibility and intervisibility conditions generally determine a lower degree of
exposure of the territory, which is reduced by the morphology of the territory itself, by the presence of
vegetation of medium and large magnitude and by occasional episodes of fog and cloudiness. The basins
visuals acquire a compact form, with limited depth of field as a result of the variations
of the relief and vegetation (SEA, 2019). Climatic conditions show landscapes that change
texture and colors according to the moderate seasonality that characterizes the central area.
Regarding the Subzone, geomorphologically speaking, the project area is located in an area of
transition between the Coastal Mountain Range and the Coastal Edge, in a sector described by Börgel (1983) as
the Central Region of the Basins and the Fluvio-Glacio-Volcanic Plain, where the coastline is generally
mixed, presenting extensive beaches of sandy accumulation combined with sections of cliffs.
On the other hand, the features of the Coastal Mountain Range, in the lower reaches of the Itata River, the mountain range
is diluted in complex reliefs, of low height, signifying a topography transformed into hills that
They advance both towards the coast and towards the interior of the territory.
The urban area of the commune of Penco is part of the Metropolitan Area of Concepción, along with 9 others
communes. The territory is mostly located on the Coastal mountain range, and the use of
Dominant soil is forestry activity (Municipality of Penco, 2012). Features
transition climates between the Mediterranean climate and the humid temperate climate that predominates towards the
south, is influenced by the effects of the coastal mountain range, where it acts as a climate screen in
relation to how temperature and precipitation behave (Municipality of Penco, 2019e); these
conditions occur in the coastal strip and in the high sectors and western slopes of the Cordillera
of the Coast, with constant humidity (INERCO, 2018). Precipitation is concentrated
preferably in winter, increasing from north to south, and from west to east, product of the presence of
frontal systems (Errázuriz, 1998).
The hydrographic system of the Commune is made up of the Penco and Lirquén Wetlands, and part of the River
Andalién, which in turn is the southern limit of the Commune. Regarding the Estero Penco, it should be noted that
This is located in the Central Urban Zone and has an approximate length of 6 km. It is born in the Zones
Altas de Penco and receives the main contribution from the natural rainwater springs (Municipality of
Penco, 2019e).
In the domain of temperate climates, of the Mediterranean type, there is the biogeographic unit “Zona
subhumid with predominance of mesó vegetation
fita, shrubby and arboreal”, which develops among the
regions of Valparaíso and Concepción (Errázuriz, 1998), and has a transition zone from the area
3-237
==================================================================================
PAGE 251
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Mediterranean to temperate from the Maule River (MNHN, 2015). In this area there are forests
typical of the Mediterranean area such as the sclerophyllous forest and also others of the hygrophilous region, such as the
oak, raulí and Coihue. These formations are currently degraded to small forests.
flanked by forestry monoculture.
The main biophysical attributes that the project environment has and that give value to the
landscape are the relief, the soil and the vegetation, although its diversity is low, its mixed character, the coverage
and permanence give landscape value to the place. Attributes like water, it is only possible to notice it
directly with respect to the sea that is within the visual field of the highest points of the
city, while, in the case of fauna, this was not declared as an attribute of interest since
They were mostly just sightings of domestic animals and birds.

Figure 3-136. Penco Beach
Source: GAC
La Planchada Fort, Regional hierarchy
It was declared a Historical Monument by D.S. No. 803 of 10/26/1977 Ministry of Education and
It is located on Penco Beach. The fort was built during the Colony, in 1687, by order
of the Governor of Chile José de Garro, as a way of defending against incursions. The construction is
carried out when the city of Concepción was still located in said place, which
would abandon decades later following a devastating earthquake in 1751. Both the area and
The fort would be abandoned from then on, which led to its progressive deterioration. The area was
gradually becoming populated after independence, until forming a new city, Penco. The Strong

Elke Observatory, regional hierarchy
Founded in 1962 by astronomer Arnoldo Bustos, it has since been a place dedicated to
dissemination of scientific astronomical knowledge in Chile and investigation of the mysteries of space.
Inside the facilities, it has an auditorium and observation dome, activities are carried out,
talks and workshops among others, with the aim that the entire community can appreciate and learn from the
universe themes. The observatory is located just over 1 km away from the area of the
project, but it is not part of its area of influence.

Plaza Los Conquistadores de Penco
Located in the heart of the civic neighborhood, Plaza Los Conquistadores, also called Plaza de Armas, is located
in what was the founding landmark of the city of Concepción, in 1550. Currently, in addition to being

amphitheater, however, the main attraction corresponds to the Penco estuary, whose channeling is located
crossed with an arched bridge and take gondola rides, imitating a small Venice. The
The location of this attraction is more than 2 km away from the project, so it is not

Figure 3-140. Estero Penco channeled in Plaza Los Conquistadores de Penco

Penco Historical Museum
Cultural space, municipal dependency and open free of charge to the community and tourists, was
inaugurated in 2016. It has a permanent exhibition that tells – through dioramas of the
artist Rodolfo Gutiérrez “Zerreitug” – the history of Penco through its main events:
Paleontology, Pre-Hispanic Occupations, Mapuche Culture, Mapuche-Spanish Encounter and Conquest,
Colony, Transfer of Concepción, Penco industrial, Education and Culture. It also offers its visitors
an Exhibition Hall with temporary museum or art samples linked to history,
culture and heritage, according to an annual program. Likewise, the Museum has a Room
Audiovisual that exhibits film cycles and a varied collection of educational videos on history, art and/or
culture in general. The location of this attraction is more than 2 km away from the project,
so it is not part of its area of influence.

iii. Tourist Routes
The “Heritage Routes” program corresponds to an initiative that depends on the Ministry of Assets
National (MBN). This program seeks to socialize fiscal spaces that have high value (social,
natural, scenic, historical or cultural) through routes passable by different means of transport
and aligned with a view of sustainable tourism.
To date, 86 routes have been enabled nationwide, integrating various locations, ecosystems,
environments and themes, equipped with minimal impact signage, as well as a guide that allows
self-guided, safe and informed tour. There are 4 types of routes: Natural, Indigenous, Cultural and
of Human Rights.
The heritage routes of the Biobío Region are the following:
- Gulf of Arauco: Carboniferous tradition of Biobío – Heritage Routes No. 67 (Cultural)
- Alto Biobío (Araucarias of the Pemehue Mountain Range) – Heritage Routes No. 43 (Natural)
- Nahuelbuta: Mountain Range, Coast and Culture – N° 36 (Cultural)
None of these routes passes through the commune of Penco, therefore, none of them have a relationship with the area of
influence of the project.

which corresponds to the “Nonguén National Park”, followed by the “Peninsula de Nature Sanctuary”.
Hualpén” 11 kilometers away and “Desembocadura Río Biobío Nature Sanctuary” 10 kilometers away.

i. Area of tourist interest
The Biobío Region has 2 Areas of Tourist Interest: “Saltos del Laja” and “Lake Lanalhue”. None
of them is related to the commune of Penco and therefore is not part of the area of influence of the
project.
ii. SERNATUR tourist destinations (2018)
According to a study coordinated between the Undersecretariat of Tourism, the central SERNATUR and its
Regional Directorates, 89 tourist destinations were delimited based on an analysis that included the
accounting for attractions, services, equipment, infrastructure, accessibility, image, resources
particular human and local identity that present the conditions conducive to attracting visitors and
develop tourist activities. The result of this study allows us to evaluate which are the main
places or destinations where visitors and tourists arrive, in addition to being able to visualize their level of development and their
tourist vocation.

According to the SERNATUR Tourist Attractions Registry, the Biobío Region registers 153 attractions,

iii. Characterization of tourism demand
The characterization of tourism demand was determined through the “Big Data for Tourism” platform.
Internal” of SERNATUR, which provides information on tourist trips with overnight stays (origin –
destination) made by residents of Chile within the country, estimated with Big Data techniques. The
Information is displayed at the level of region, tourist destination and commune. The series starts from January 2019
from now on, on an annual and monthly basis.
The method considers the guidelines of the World Tourism Organization to transform large
volumes of data from mobile phone signal transactions, in aggregate and
anonymized, through a series of purification algorithms, in national statistics,
in accordance with personal data privacy regulations.
3-256
==================================================================================
PAGE 270
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
The concept of usual environment is a fundamental axis in tourism statistics: "so that
Consider a tourist trip, the trip must take the traveler outside his or her usual environment." For this, the
World Tourism Organization suggests establishing criteria to determine the “usual environment”; between
which is the “frequency of the trip”. Under this consideration, and in order to know in
depth the flow of domestic tourism, the information is presented from 2 angles: “tourist trips
frequent” and “infrequent tourist trips”.
- Frequent tourist trips: The trip is made with a maximum frequency of 3 times to the same destination
main during the month of analysis.
- Infrequent tourist trips: The trip is not repeated to the same main destination in 3 months. Also
They could be called "occasional tourist trips."
For the following analysis, data for infrequent tourist trips will be considered, with data

3.20.6 Conclusions
The sector where the Mining Development Project for the Extraction of Clays for the Production of
Concentrated Rare Earths, corresponds to the commune of Penco and Concepción, Biobío Region,
specifically located in the Coihueco Fund sector, located on part of the coastal mountain range.
Its main access is via Route 150, in front of the town of La Greda. An important part of the
dynamic
tourism of the commune of Penco is to be part of the SERNATUR Tourist Destination (2018)
“Concepción and surroundings” which includes a large part of the Metropolitan Area of Concepción and has a
consolidated level of development.
The Landscape Value was analyzed from 2 sources, in the first case, taking the results obtained
in the Landscape Value Baseline of this EIA, which resulted in a Landscape Value
and Medium visual quality.
The Cultural Value was determined low, since no cultural attractions were identified within the area.
of influence.
On the other hand, the Heritage Value was evaluated as Medium, since, within the area of influence,
They develop recreational and sports activities.
Regarding the attraction of visitors, it is relevant to mention the context in which the commune is inserted,
since Penco is part of the Metropolitan Area of Concepción, which is part of the Tourist Destination
“Concepción and surroundings.” At the local level, the commune of Penco receives nearly 40 thousand tourist trips, the
which happen throughout the year, mainly in the summer season, where it reaches 7 thousand
monthly visitors.

3.21 Use of territory
3.21.1 Introduction
The Mining Development Project of Clay Extraction for the Production of Earth Concentrate
Raras (hereinafter the Project) is located in the Biobío Region, Province of Concepción. The facilities
of the Project are located in the communes of Penco and Concepción. The Project consists of the construction
and operation of a mining site, along with a Regolith-type Material processing plant, with
strong presence of clays. Regolith is material from a highly weathered rock,
called “Clays to be processed”, with the presence of Lanthanides adsorbed in the clay minerals.
This report provides the characterization of Territory Use in the context of the EIA Project.
of Mining Development of Clay Extraction for Production of Rare Earth Concentrate (in
hereinafter “the Project”). This analysis includes the description of (i) Current and potential land use, (ii) land
planned, (iii) economic and productive activities, and (iv) the relevant constructions, whose main
The objective is to evaluate the potential effects that could be produced by the project on the
sociocultural elements of the communities or human groups that use the territory. According to
what is established in Law No. 19,300 of General Bases of the Environment and the Regulation of the System of
Environmental Assessment D.S. No. 40/2012.
3.21.2 Objective
3.21.2.1 General Objective
Evaluate the potential effects that could be produced by project works on the elements
sociocultural aspects of the communities or human groups that use the territory.
3.21.2.2 Specific Objectives
• Characterize the soil in the Project area based on the Use Capacity Classes.
of soil and
Current use.
• Describe and analyze the Territorial Planning and Territorial Ordering Instruments
present in the area where the works and parts of the project will be located in their different
hierarchies and scales of application.
• Indicate the main economic and productive characteristics of the area of ​​influence.
• Describe and characterize the infrastructure and equipment present in the area of ​​influence.

3.21.4 Methodology
3.21.4.1 Actual land use
i. Identification of current land use
To establish current land use, several sources of information can be used. One of them is
based on the study carried out by the National Forestry Corporation (CONAF) “Cadastro and Evaluation
of the Native Vegetative Resources of Chile”. This registry is periodically updated by CONAF,
through continuity projects of regional scope, whose objective is to monitor changes in use
of the soil that occurred between measurement periods and identify their causes.
Land use can be defined as the different uses that humans can make of the land or
the surface where its activities are supported. In accordance with the contents indicated in the Guide for
the Description of Territory Use in the SEIA (2013), the categorization of uses can adopt the
established in the General Urban Planning and Construction Ordinance, which distinguishes the following types of
land uses:
Table 3-44. Land uses according to the General Urban Planning and Construction Ordinance (OGUC)
Land uses
Residential Infrastructure
Green area equipment
Productive Activities Public Space
Source: OGUC
Meanwhile, for the Cadastre and Evaluation of Native Vegetative Resources of Chile, land use is
defined based on the following categories:
Table 3-45. Land uses according to Vegetable Resources Cadastre
Land uses
Urban and industrial Wetlands
Agricultural Land Areas Without Vegetation
Grasslands and Shrubs Snow and Glaciers
Forests Bodies of Water
Source: CONAF
In the case of this project, the definition of land use will be carried out based on the
photointerpretation of current satellite images, in order to contextualize the place of
location in more detail.

ii. Identification of potential land use
To prepare this section there are mainly two sources of information, through
through a study
specific to the soil component, from bibliographic resources or from the cross-referencing of information
with the cartographic resources available for the area prepared by the Resource Information Center
Natural (CIREN). In both cases, the object is to determine what the potential use of the land is, and whether
This is consistent with the activities to be developed by the project, which determines the
Land Use Capacity.
The land use capacity corresponds to a method for the description and classification of soils and the
establishment of the classes of usability of them, mainly oriented to the use
silvoagropecuario. This method is adapted to Chile as set out in the document Guideline for
Soil Studies (SAG, 2011).
There are eight Land Use Capacity Classes, identified with Roman numerals (I to VIII), which
They express the increasing degree of limitations or permanent irrigation of the soil. The first four classes
They identify arable soils (I-IV) and non-arable soils (V-VIII). A subclass is added to these classes that
correspond to 4 letters (e, w, s, cl28) that accompany the numbers and represent the problems
dominants that affect the soil.

iii. Land use planned by Planning, Ordering and
Territorial Management
a) Identification of Territorial Planning Instruments
The Territorial Planning Instruments are legal tools defined by DFL No. 458, of 1978.
from the Ministry of Housing and Urban Planning to
through the General Law of Urban Planning and Construction (LGUC),
whose function is to guide or regulate, as the case may be, the development of Urban Centers, and therefore
opposition, also all those territories that are outside urbanized areas. Each
instrument has a particular scope of action, covering different scales and indicating different
subjects and provisions. Under this provision, the existing IPTs are:
• Regional Urban Development Plan (PRDU)
• Metropolitan Intercommunal Regulatory Plan (PRI or PRM)
• Communal Regulatory Plan (PRC)
• Sectional Plan (PS)
• Urban Limit (LU)
For an instrument to be in force, it must be promulgated by the Regional Government
corresponding, and published in the Official Gazette as a Decree, otherwise the document does not count
with legal validity, and therefore has no normative power.
3-269
==================================================================================
PAGE 283
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
In order to analyze the respective documents, it is necessary to have the publications of the Journal
Official, the Explanatory Report, and ideally also with a vector file of type Kmz or shp to
to be able to visualize the zoning of the instrument, and also to be able to cross-reference the information with the area
of the respective project.
Identification of Territorial Planning Instruments
To describe the area of influence of the project, it is also necessary to incorporate the instruments
of Territorial Planning, which within the framework of the SEIA corresponds to the areas of:
• Regional Territorial Planning Plan (PROT)
• Indigenous Development Areas (ADI)
• Coastal Edge Zoning (ZBC)
In these, certain projected or planned land use zones are proposed, which must be
related or superimposed on the area of influence of the project in order to predict environmental impacts.

present in the area of influence is to collect background information bibliographically and online
necessary background information that allows characterizing a particular site, and there may be a crossover of data
with field visits and primary sources, the latter coming from the study carried out in Chapter 3
Section D.
Within the search for online information, there are the pages of the municipalities and
respective regional governments, territorial planning instruments and development strategies;
productive censuses, cadastres, local media and in some cases articles or reports
of title that can enrich the background on the economic and productive activities that are carried out.
develop in one place.

of the area of influence, such as infrastructure, housing, equipment or other use, which is necessary to know

The land uses are the following:
ZE-1: Preferred Commercial Equipment Zone
According to the PRC Ordinance, permitted uses are identified as those referring to Residential, Equipment
of all types (except Cemeteries, Crematoriums, Prisons, Military Compounds, Stadiums and Zoos).
Furthermore, regarding prohibited uses, Hazardous Productive Activities are mentioned, except for
existing and expressly contemplated in the PRMS, Landfills and Sanitary Landfills of Solid Waste
Domestic and Industrial and Transfer Centers, the latter except in zones ZEE-1, ZEE-3 and
ZEE-4, Extraction of Aggregates and Manufacturing of Bricks (with the exception of the extraction of aggregates and/or stones from
beds of water courses authorized by the competent services), Water Treatment Plants
Services that operate with open lagoons and exposure of surfaces to the environment, dangerous infrastructure
and/or highly polluting.
ZP-3: Landscape Protection Zone
According to the PRC Ordinance, permitted uses are identified as those referring to Green Areas (parks,
viewpoints, walking tours), Equipment (worship and culture, sports, education, recreation, health,
security and services.
Regarding prohibited uses, Hazardous Productive Activities are mentioned, except for existing ones.
and expressly contemplated in the PRMS, Landfills and Sanitary Landfills of Solid Waste

According to the previous planning, it is possible to identify the following zonings and their respective
land use conditions:
ZD: Drainage Zones (part of the General Zoning of Protection Areas and
Risk)
The ZD is part of the Metropolitan System of Green Areas and Protected Zones, and corresponds to
those areas excluded from urban development, whose purpose is linked to the protection of normal
surface water runoff. Included in this zone are: river beds, estuaries, bottoms and slopes.
bottom of streams.
The uses allowed in this zoning correspond to: Forestry (protection only), Mining (only
extraction of aggregates from watercourse beds, authorized by the competent services).
Furthermore, it is important to mention that the ZDs located within the urban limits that determine the
metropolitan extension area, must contemplate a protection edge on both banks,
intended for green areas, walks and parks, it will be defined through specific projects. On the other hand,
Infrastructure works that cross these areas must consider the necessary design so that
the normal runoff of rainwater and their respective water systems is not blocked.
ZEHM: Mixed Housing Extension Zone (part of the General Zoning of the Area
Consolidated Urban):
The ZEHM correspond to those areas destined to absorb metropolitan urban growth,
whose predominant use corresponds to the residential type, with the presence of varied equipment and that
be complementary.
The uses allowed in this zoning correspond to: Housing, Equipment, Industrial (qualified
as harmless by the competent authority), Transportation Infrastructure. Additionally, they will be allowed
industry, storage and workshop activities, rated as annoying and informed
favorably by the Health Service, that is, with its impacts mitigated or risks controlled.
ZEP: Slope Extension Zone (part of the General Zoning of the Urban Area
Consolidated):
It corresponds to the slopes of hills in which, mainly due to their topography, slopes, value
landscape, as well as for its structural importance in the definition and determination of the areas
urbanizable areas and the identity of the metropolitan area, development or
intensive radish, with
in order to protect the following attributes: terrain morphology, associated natural risks, vegetation
existing and the landscape framework.
3-283
==================================================================================
PAGE 297
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
The uses allowed in this zoning correspond to: Housing, Equipment (recreation and
tourism, culture, educational, health, sports and commerce) and Forestry (protection only).
The occupation and use of the land in this area must consider the following special conditions:
Arborization with ornamental and/or native species; Prohibition of earthworks that alter
significantly the topographic characteristics of the land, having to ensure the maintenance of the value
landscape of the sector. For road projects, the slopes generated must consider the construction works.
necessary protection to prevent collapses or slides; The unoccupied areas of the property
due to constructions, they must be kept planted with trees (PRMC Ordinance, Year 2003).
ZHM: Mixed Housing Zone (part of the General Zoning of the Urban Area
Consolidated):
It corresponds to those areas classified as consolidated and/or recognized by the current PRC, whose
The destination is preferably mixed housing type, that is, housing with the presence of a variety of
complementary equipment at regional, intercommunal, and local level, in addition to other land uses
such as the industrial type (of a harmless nature), which tends to coexist with residential use
predominant.
The uses allowed in this zoning correspond to: Housing, Equipment, Infrastructure
Land transport (rail and road) and river transport, Industrial (industry and harmless storage;
harmless or annoying workshops, qualified by the competent authority).
In addition, they will be allowed (on an exceptional basis and provided that the communal or sectional regulatory plan so permits)
establishes), industrial and storage activities, classified as annoying, and informed
favorably by the respective Health Service, that is, with its mitigated impacts or risks
controlled. Without prejudice to the above, these activities must optimize their production processes
in order to improve its environmental rating (PRMC Ordinance, Year 2003).
ZIS: Area of Forestry and Agricultural Interest (part of the general Zoning of the Rural Area
Metropolitan):
This area corresponds to the territories whose soil characteristics are suitable for forestry and agriculture,
require regulation.
The uses allowed in this zoning correspond to: Housing (complementary to the development of
the activity), Agriculture, Forestry, Mining.
Additionally, with favorable reports from the competent bodies, the following uses may be authorized:
Housing (only housing complexes with state subsidy), Equipment, Industrial (qualified as
harmless, annoying and/or dangerous by the competent authority), Transportation Infrastructure, Warehouses
and/or solid waste treatment plants.

b) Territorial Planning Instruments
In accordance with the definition used by the Guide for the Description of Territory Use in the SEIA (SEA
2013) “territorial planning” is considered a process and a planning instrument with a
technical-political-administrative character, with which it is intended to organize the long-term occupation of the
territory, taking into account the potential and limitations of each spatial unit
analyzed. These instruments aim to specify a territorial model for the future, through different
strategies that allow achieving the defined objectives.
Based on the above, the Territorial Planning Instruments that are distinguished within the SEIA are
the Regional Territorial Planning Plans (PROT), the Coastal Edge Zoning (ZBC) and the
Indigenous Development Areas (ADI). The above is presented in summary in Table 3-50.
Table 3-50. Applicability of Territorial Planning Instruments
Territorial Planning Instruments Validity and/or applicability of the Project

3.21.5.3 Economic and Productive Activities
a) Biobío Region
The Biobío Region corresponds to one of the most important in the country, along with those in which
They carry out activities such as mining or other types of economic activities that are fundamental in
the national economy.
From the regional point of view, there is a territorial dynamic in relation to the use destined for activities
productive that is very dynamic and diverse, with industries associated with traditional agriculture,
steel industry, forestry activity and with it the production of cellulose, generation of electricity through
different mechanisms29. Based on the above, it is possible to determine that the economic activities and
productive activities that are developed in the region are mostly extractive in nature, depending
of natural resources and their respective subsequent processing.

Commune of Concepción and Penco
As for the commune of Penco, the activities are mainly linked to fishing,
forestry and port activity, but the
glass production.
On the other hand, the commune of Concepción corresponds to one of the largest in Chile, following in the
list to Santiago. For this reason, both Concepción and Penco are part of the Regulatory Plan
Metropolitan of Concepción, since both communes along with Tomé, Talcahuano, Hualpén,
Chiguayante, Hualqui, Santa Juana, San Pedro de La Paz, Coronel and Lota, form the second agglomerate
largest metropolitan area in the country, where not only more than 500,000
inhabitants30, but the territory must also be planned in order to promote coexistence
between these multiple dynamics that develop in the same territory.
Finally, it should be mentioned that in this dynamic and diverse territory not only activities coexist
productive extractives on a large scale, but traditional activities are also developed, such as
peasant agriculture or artisanal fishing. This coexistence between both productivity scales,
They provide a higher level of complexity, both social and cultural, to the region.

3.21.6 Conclusions
In relation to the current use of the land, to the location of the Project, it is located in the
communes of Penco and Concepción. With respect to the location area and the current activities that
develop in the place, it is possible to determine (after the application of the
photointerpretation) that the productive and extractive activities present in the area correspond
mainly to eucalyptus and pine forestry activity.
On the other hand, in relation to Planned Land Use, in the Project area two areas are identified.
territorial planning instruments of different administrative scales: Communal Regulatory Plan of
Penco and the Metropolitan Regulatory Plan of Concepción (at the Metropolitan Intercommunal level).
The main activities are extractive or primary, such as forestry, agriculture (both
traditional and agroindustrial), fishing (both artisanal and industrial scale), and other types of
activities that are characteristic of the area.
Based on the background presented previously and the analysis that was developed in this
study, it is possible to determine that the Project is located in an area with active use in the area
productive economic, but also social and cultural. Even so, specifically in the area of influence
of the Project, corresponds to a segment of the communal and regional territory that has been greatly intervened, not only
from extractive activity, but also from the installation of infrastructures of different types.

3.22 Projects or activities with current RCA
3.22.1 Introduction
In accordance with the provisions of article 12 bis of Law 20,417, which modifies Law 19,300 and literal b of
article 19 of the regulations of the am impact evaluation system
biental (D.S. N°40/2012 MMA), the
Projects must present “The necessary background information that justifies the non-existence of those
effects, characteristics or circumstances of article 11 of the Law that may give rise to the need for
carry out an Environmental Impact Study.” In accordance with such provision and in accordance with the
indicated in literal b.1 of article 19, which establishes that, within the necessary background to
an Environmental Impact Statement, it must include “The determination and justification of the area of
influence of the project or activity, including a general description thereof, as provided
indicated in article 18 letter d) of the regulations.”
Thus, considering the above and, in order to carry out an appropriate characterization of the area of influence, it is
uses as a reference what is described in article 18 literal e.11, which instructs that projects
will present a baseline that includes, when appropriate, “Projects or activities that have
Current Environmental Qualification Resolution, even when they are not operating.”
In accordance with the above, the present section describes the projects located near the area of influence
of the project and who have a current RCA.
3.22.2 Methodology
Projects with a current Environmental Qualification Resolution (RCA) were identified, whether they were
Environmental Impact Statements (DIA) or Environmental Impact Studies (EIA), including their
spatial distribution within the territory close to the area where the present works will be located
Project.
To identify projects with RCA close to the Project, information was collected from all projects
entered the SEIA using the project search service by region, in addition there was access to the
downloadable information, on the same website, in Excel and KMZ31 format. The search was carried out in
January 2024. The search criteria used were:
• Geographic location: projects from the Biobío Region that had works or
activities within the limits of the Communes of Concepción and Penco. Specifically, it
selected projects located on a circular surface of 9 km radius (centered on the area
of the project under evaluation).
31 http://www.sea.gob.cl/
3-291
==================================================================================
PAGE 305
==================================================================================
Chapter 3 Baseline (Section C)
Cultural Heritage
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
• Date of presentation to the SEIA: projects that were presented between 1994 were searched.
and 2024.
• Project status: projects that were in Approved status were searched.
• Productive sector: all productive sectors were considered
The result of the project search was analyzed by type of entry to the SEIA (DIA or EIA), region, commune
and productive sector. Then, the existing significant impacts of these projects were identified,
considering the phase in which the impacts are generated, the affected component and its geographical location.
For this, only projects that have carried out Environmental Impact Studies (EIA) were considered, since
Environmental Impact Statements (DIA) are those where compliance with the
current environmental legislation and the existence of those effects, characteristics
or circumstances of Article 11 of Law No. 19,300, so said projects do not have impacts
significant in the environment.
3.22.3 Results
According to the search carried out, 66 projects were identified with RCA approved in the System of
Environmental Impact Assessment (SEIA), in the Biobío Region, communes of Concepción and Penco since
1994 to 2024. The location of these is shown in Figure 3-160. Annex 3C-59 presents the
location of projects in digital format.

3.22.4 Conclusions
The Project area “Mining Development of Clay Extraction for Production of Concentrated
Rare Earths” is located in the Communes of Penco and Concepción, Province of Concepción, Region of
Biobío, specifically in a sector where there are various productive activities: energy,
industrial, sanitation and manufacturing facilities, among others. According to the information reviewed, the
components that receive significant impacts most frequently are: Air Quality, Environment
Human, Aquatic Flora and Fauna, Soil, Terrestrial Flora and Vegetation and Terrestrial Fauna.
Specifically, in the Biobío Region, mainly in the communes of Penco and Concepción,
identified 66 projects within a 9 km radius with current RCA, in the period included
from 1994 to 2024. Of these 66 projects, 57 were entered as Impact Statement
(DIA) and 9 as Environmental Impact Study (EIA), with emphasis on the latter for the
determination of significant impacts.
